Section 1: Java Fundamentals

Java Overview

Java is a high-level, object-oriented programming language developed by Sun Microsystems (now Oracle) in 1995. It is designed for building platform-independent applications — from enterprise backends to mobile apps (Android) to test automation frameworks like Selenium, TestNG, and Cucumber.

What is Java?

Java is a compiled-then-interpreted language. Source code (.java) is compiled into platform-neutral bytecode (.class), which the JVM executes on any operating system. This makes Java ideal for cross-platform test suites that run on Windows CI agents, macOS developer machines, and Linux Docker containers without code changes.

Why Java for QA Automation?

  • Industry standard — Selenium WebDriver, TestNG, JUnit, Rest Assured, and Cucumber all have first-class Java support.
  • Rich ecosystem — Maven/Gradle, ExtentReports, Log4j, Jackson, and Apache POI for data-driven testing.
  • Strong typing — catches errors at compile time, reducing flaky test code.
  • OOP design — Page Object Model, Factory patterns, and layered frameworks map naturally to Java.
  • Enterprise adoption — most SDET/Senior QA roles expect Java proficiency.

Platform Independence & "Write Once, Run Anywhere" (WORA)

Java achieves platform independence through bytecode and the JVM. You compile once; the JVM on each platform translates bytecode to native machine instructions. Your Selenium tests compiled on Windows run identically on a Linux Jenkins agent — only the browser/driver binaries differ.

Interview Tip: WORA means bytecode portability, not absolute zero configuration. You still need a JVM and OS-specific native drivers (ChromeDriver, geckodriver) on each machine.

JDK vs JRE vs JVM

ComponentPurposeContainsExampleWho Needs It
JVM (Java Virtual Machine)Runtime engine that executes bytecodeClass loader, memory areas, GC, execution engineHotSpot JVM (default since JDK 9)End users running Java apps/tests
JRE (Java Runtime Environment)Provides runtime libraries to run Java programsJVM + core libraries (java.lang, java.util, etc.)java -jar tests.jarQA running pre-built test JARs on CI without compiling
JDK (Java Development Kit)Full toolkit to develop, compile, debug, and run JavaJRE + compiler (javac), debugger (jdb), javadoc, jarJDK 17, JDK 21SDETs writing and building automation frameworks

JVM Architecture

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     JVM ARCHITECTURE                            │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  ┌──────────────┐                                               │
│  │ ClassLoader  │──► Loads .class files into Method Area         │
│  │  Subsystem   │    (Bootstrap → Extension → Application)      │
│  └──────┬───────┘                                               │
│         │                                                       │
│         ▼                                                       │
│  ┌──────────────┐    ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ Method Area  │    │              HEAP                     │  │
│  │ (MetaSpace)  │    │  ┌─────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐  │  │
│  │ Class data,  │    │  │ Young   │  │    Old Gen       │  │  │
│  │ static vars, │    │  │  Gen    │  │  (Long-lived     │  │  │
│  │ constant pool│    │  │ Eden +  │  │   objects)       │  │  │
│  └──────────────┘    │  │ Survivor│  └──────────────────┘  │  │
│                      │  └─────────┘                          │  │
│  Per Thread:         └─────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│  ┌──────────────┐                                               │
│  │    STACK     │  Local vars, method calls, partial results   │
│  │  (LIFO frames)│                                              │
│  └──────────────┘                                               │
│  ┌──────────────┐                                               │
│  │ PC Register  │  Address of current executing instruction     │
│  └──────────────┘                                               │
│  ┌──────────────┐                                               │
│  │ Native Method│  Native (C/C++) method calls                 │
│  │    Stack     │                                               │
│  └──────────────┘                                               │
│                                                                 │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │              EXECUTION ENGINE                             │  │
│  │  Interpreter │ JIT Compiler │ Garbage Collector           │  │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Java Architecture — Source to Execution

  ┌─────────────┐     javac      ┌─────────────┐     java      ┌─────────────┐
  │  Source     │  ──────────►   │  Bytecode   │  ─────────►  │    JVM      │
  │  (.java)    │   (Compiler)   │  (.class)   │  (ClassLoader)│             │
  └─────────────┘                └─────────────┘               └──────┬──────┘
  LoginTest.java                   LoginTest.class                      │
  BasePage.java                    BasePage.class                       ▼
                                                              ┌─────────────────┐
                                                              │ Execution Engine │
                                                              │ (Interpreter +   │
                                                              │  JIT Compiler)   │
                                                              └────────┬────────┘
                                                                       ▼
                                                              ┌─────────────────┐
                                                              │  Machine Code   │
                                                              │  (OS-specific)  │
                                                              └─────────────────┘

Compilation Process

// Step 1: Write source code
// File: HelloTest.java
public class HelloTest {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println("Automation Ready!");
    }
}

// Step 2: Compile — produces HelloTest.class (bytecode)
// Command: javac HelloTest.java

// Step 3: Run — JVM loads and executes bytecode
// Command: java HelloTest
// Output: Automation Ready!

Key commands for SDETs:

  • javac *.java — compile all source files
  • java com.company.tests.LoginTest — run by fully qualified class name
  • jar cf tests.jar *.class — package compiled tests
  • mvn clean test — Maven compiles and runs TestNG suites (standard in frameworks)

Memory Management

Stack vs Heap

AspectStackHeap
StoresMethod frames, local primitives, object referencesActual objects and instance/static variables
SizeSmaller, fixed per thread (~1 MB default)Larger, shared across threads (configurable via -Xmx)
SpeedFast (LIFO allocation/deallocation)Slower (dynamic allocation)
Memory managementAutomatic when method returns (pop frame)Garbage Collector reclaims unused objects
Thread safetyEach thread has its own stackShared — requires synchronization for thread safety
Example in automationint timeout = 10; local in wait methodWebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver(); object on heap

Garbage Collection Basics

GC automatically reclaims heap memory from objects with no live references. When your test finishes and the WebDriver reference goes out of scope (or is set to null), GC eventually frees that memory.

  • Minor GC — cleans Young Generation (Eden/Survivor); frequent, fast
  • Major/Full GC — cleans Old Generation; less frequent, can cause pauses
  • Unreachable objects — no reference chain from GC roots (stack refs, static fields, JNI refs)

GC Algorithms

  • Serial GC (-XX:+UseSerialGC) — single thread; small apps, low memory
  • Parallel GC (-XX:+UseParallelGC) — multi-threaded; throughput-focused; default for server-class machines
  • G1 GC (-XX:+UseG1GC) — default since JDK 9; divides heap into regions; predictable pauses; ideal for large parallel test suites
CI Tip: Parallel test runs consume heap fast. Set -Xmx2g -XX:+UseG1GC in your Maven Surefire or Jenkins JVM args to avoid OOM during large suites.

Java Features

  • Object-Oriented — everything (except primitives) is an object; supports encapsulation, inheritance, polymorphism, abstraction
  • Platform Independent — bytecode + JVM = WORA
  • Robust — strong typing, exception handling, no pointer arithmetic
  • Secure — bytecode verification, SecurityManager (deprecated in 17), sandboxing
  • Multithreaded — built-in Thread class; run parallel tests with TestNG parallel="methods"
  • Architecture Neutral — same bytecode runs on 32-bit or 64-bit JVMs

Data Types Preview

Java has 8 primitive types (byte, short, int, long, float, double, char, boolean) and reference types (String, arrays, classes, interfaces). Primitives store values directly; references store memory addresses pointing to heap objects.

Naming Conventions

ElementConventionExample (Automation)

JDK Versions Timeline — What Matters for Automation

VersionReleaseKey Features for SDETsStatus
Java 82014Lambda expressions, Streams API, Optional, default interface methods — still common in legacy frameworksLTS (extended support)
Java 112018var in lambdas, HTTP Client API, removed Java EE modules — widely used LTS in enterprise CILTS
Java 172021Sealed classes, pattern matching for switch, strong encapsulation — current industry standard for new projectsLTS (recommended)
Java 212023Virtual threads, sequenced collections, record patterns — emerging in modern frameworksLTS (latest)
Interview Answer: "For automation I prefer JDK 17 LTS — stable, long support, compatible with Selenium 4.x, TestNG 7.x, and Maven. Java 8 is legacy but still appears in older codebases. Java 21 virtual threads help high-concurrency API test runners."

Interview Q&A — Section 1

Q1: What is the difference between JDK, JRE, and JVM?

A: JVM executes bytecode. JRE = JVM + runtime libraries (enough to run apps). JDK = JRE + development tools like javac (needed to write and compile code). SDETs need JDK; CI runners executing pre-built JARs may only need JRE.

Q2: Explain "Write Once, Run Anywhere."

A: Java source compiles to platform-neutral bytecode. Any OS with a compatible JVM can run that bytecode. The JVM handles OS-specific details. In automation, the same test JAR runs on Windows, macOS, and Linux agents.

Q3: What is bytecode?

A: Intermediate instruction set produced by javac, stored in .class files. It is neither source code nor native machine code — the JVM interprets or JIT-compiles it to native instructions at runtime.

Q4: Stack vs Heap — where is a WebDriver object stored?

A: The reference variable driver is on the stack (local variable in a method). The actual ChromeDriver object lives on the heap. When the method ends, the stack reference is popped; the heap object becomes eligible for GC.

Q5: What is Garbage Collection?

A: Automatic memory management that reclaims heap objects no longer reachable from GC roots. Prevents memory leaks in long-running test suites. Triggered automatically; can be hinted with System.gc() but never guaranteed.

Q6: What is the main method signature and why is it required?

A: public static void main(String[] args) — JVM entry point. public for JVM access, static so JVM can call without creating an object, void returns nothing, String[] args for command-line params. TestNG/JUnit don't need main — their runners invoke tests directly.

Q7: What is JIT compilation?

A: Just-In-Time compiler converts frequently executed bytecode to native machine code at runtime for performance. Hot methods in your framework (waits, element lookups) benefit from JIT after warm-up runs.

Q8: Can Java run without main method?

A: Yes. Applets (deprecated), servlets, TestNG test classes, and Spring Boot apps use other entry points. TestNG uses annotations like @Test discovered by the TestNG runner.

Q9: What is the role of ClassLoader?

A: Loads .class files into Method Area. Bootstrap loads core JDK classes, Extension loads extension libs, Application loads classpath classes (your test framework). Custom ClassLoaders exist for plugin architectures.

Q10: Why is Java popular for test automation?

A: Mature Selenium bindings, strong typing, excellent IDE support (IntelliJ), Maven/Gradle dependency management, enterprise adoption, OOP for Page Object Model, and vast hiring demand for Java SDETs.

Q11: What happens when you run java LoginTest?

A: JVM starts → ClassLoader loads LoginTest.class → bytecode verified → main (or TestNG runner) invoked → Execution Engine interprets/JIT-compiles → native code runs on OS.

Q12: What is -Xmx and -Xms?

A: JVM heap flags. -Xms = initial heap size, -Xmx = maximum heap size. Example: -Xms512m -Xmx2g. Critical for parallel test execution to avoid OutOfMemoryError.

Q13: Is Java compiled or interpreted?

A: Both. Source is compiled to bytecode by javac (compile-time). JVM interprets bytecode at runtime and JIT-compiles hot code to native machine code. Hence "compiled-then-interpreted."

Q14: What is MetaSpace (Java 8+)?

A: Replaced PermGen. Stores class metadata in native memory (not heap). Grows dynamically. PermGen OutOfMemoryErrors from loading too many classes (dynamic proxies in frameworks) are largely resolved.

Q15: Difference between .java and .class files?

A: .java is human-readable source code you write. .class is compiled bytecode the JVM executes. One .java file typically produces one .class file (inner classes produce additional .class files).

Q16: What JVM do you use in production CI?

A: HotSpot (default Oracle/OpenJDK JVM). Amazon Corretto, Eclipse Temurin, and Azul Zulu are popular distributions. All implement the same JVM spec — choose based on org licensing and support policies.

Section 2: OOPS Concepts

Class

Definition

A class is a blueprint or template that defines the structure (fields) and behavior (methods) of objects. It encapsulates data and operations into a single unit.

Real-World Analogy

A house blueprint defines rooms, doors, and layout. You don't live in the blueprint — you build actual houses from it. Similarly, a LoginPage class defines locators and actions; each test creates a real instance to interact with the browser.

Java Code Example

public class LoginPage {
    // Fields (state)
    private WebDriver driver;
    private By usernameField = By.id("username");
    private By passwordField = By.id("password");
    private By loginButton   = By.id("loginBtn");

    // Default constructor (no-args)
    public LoginPage() {
        this.driver = DriverFactory.getDriver();
    }

    // Parameterized constructor
    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
    }

    // Copy constructor
    public LoginPage(LoginPage other) {
        this.driver = other.driver;
    }

    // Methods (behavior)
    public void enterUsername(String username) {
        driver.findElement(usernameField).sendKeys(username);
    }

    public void enterPassword(String password) {
        driver.findElement(passwordField).sendKeys(password);
    }

    public void clickLogin() {
        driver.findElement(loginButton).click();
    }

    public void login(String user, String pass) {
        enterUsername(user);
        enterPassword(pass);
        clickLogin();
    }
}

Constructor Types

  • Default — no-args; JVM provides one if none defined
  • Parameterized — accepts arguments to initialize fields
  • Copy — creates new object from existing object's state

this Keyword

Refers to the current object instance. Used to: differentiate fields from parameters, call other constructors (this()), return current instance for method chaining.

Selenium Usage

Page Object classes are the cornerstone of maintainable automation. Each page/component gets its own class with locators as private fields and user actions as public methods.

Interview Q&A — Class

Q: Can a class have multiple constructors?
A: Yes — constructor overloading. Same class name, different parameter lists. JVM selects based on arguments passed at instantiation.

Object

Definition

An object is an instance of a class — a concrete entity in memory with its own state (field values) and behavior (methods).

Real-World Analogy

If Car is a class, your specific Toyota Camry is an object — it has actual color, mileage, and license plate values.

Java Code Example

// Class definition
public class DashboardPage {
    private WebDriver driver;

    public DashboardPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
    }

    public String getWelcomeMessage() {
        return driver.findElement(By.id("welcome")).getText();
    }
}

// Object creation
public class LoginTest {
    @Test
    public void testSuccessfulLogin() {
        WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();          // Object 1
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);      // Object 2
        loginPage.login("admin", "pass123");

        DashboardPage dashboard = new DashboardPage(driver); // Object 3
        Assert.assertTrue(dashboard.getWelcomeMessage().contains("Welcome"));
    }
}

Key Concepts

  • new keyword allocates memory on heap and invokes constructor
  • Reference variable (e.g., loginPage) on stack points to heap object
  • Multiple references can point to same object
  • null means reference points to nothing — calling methods causes NullPointerException

Selenium Usage

LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);
loginPage.login("testuser", "password");
// loginPage is a reference; the LoginPage object holds driver state and locators

Encapsulation

Definition

Encapsulation bundles data (fields) and methods that operate on that data within a class, restricting direct access via access modifiers. Data hiding through private fields + public getters/setters.

Real-World Analogy

A TV remote exposes buttons (public interface) but hides internal circuitry (private). You press "power" without knowing how the transistor switches work.

Complete Code Example

public class ConfigReader {
    // Private fields — hidden from outside
    private static Properties properties = new Properties();
    private static final String CONFIG_PATH = "src/test/resources/config.properties";

    // Private constructor — prevent instantiation (utility class pattern)
    private ConfigReader() {}

    // Controlled public access
    public static String getProperty(String key) {
        loadPropertiesIfNeeded();
        return properties.getProperty(key);
    }

    public static String getBaseUrl() {
        return getProperty("base.url");
    }

    public static int getTimeout() {
        return Integer.parseInt(getProperty("timeout.seconds"));
    }

    private static void loadPropertiesIfNeeded() {
        if (properties.isEmpty()) {
            try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(CONFIG_PATH)) {
                properties.load(fis);
            } catch (IOException e) {
                throw new FrameworkException("Failed to load config", e);
            }
        }
    }
}

// Encapsulated WebDriver in BaseTest
public class BaseTest {
    private WebDriver driver;  // private — tests can't accidentally reassign

    protected WebDriver getDriver() {
        return driver;
    }

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setUp() {
        driver = DriverFactory.createDriver("chrome");
        driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void tearDown() {
        if (driver != null) {
            driver.quit();
        }
    }
}

Selenium Usage

Page Objects hide locator details (private By fields). Tests call loginPage.login(user, pass) without knowing element IDs changed from #user to #username.

Interview Q&A — Encapsulation

Q: How does encapsulation help test maintenance?
A: Locator changes happen in one class. Tests remain unchanged. Reduces duplication and prevents tests from directly manipulating WebDriver internals.

Inheritance

Definition

Inheritance allows a class (child/subclass) to acquire fields and methods of another class (parent/superclass) using extends. Establishes an IS-A relationship.

Real-World Analogy

A ElectricCar IS-A Car — it inherits wheels, engine concept, but adds battery-specific behavior.

Types of Inheritance in Java

  • Single — one parent, one child: LoginTest extends BaseTest
  • Multilevel — chain: SmokeTest → RegressionTest → BaseTest
  • Hierarchical — multiple children, one parent: LoginTest and SearchTest both extend BaseTest
  • Multiple inheritance of classes — NOT supported in Java

Complete Inheritance Hierarchy

// Parent / Super class
public class BaseTest {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected Logger logger = LogManager.getLogger(this.getClass());

    @BeforeMethod
    @Parameters({"browser"})
    public void setUp(@Optional("chrome") String browser) {
        driver = DriverFactory.createDriver(browser);
        driver.manage().window().maximize();
        logger.info("Browser launched: " + browser);
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void tearDown() {
        if (driver != null) {
            driver.quit();
            logger.info("Browser closed");
        }
    }

    protected void takeScreenshot(String name) {
        // shared utility for all tests
    }
}

// Child / Sub class
public class LoginTest extends BaseTest {

    private LoginPage loginPage;

    @BeforeMethod
    public void initPage() {
        loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);  // driver inherited from BaseTest
    }

    @Test
    public void verifyValidLogin() {
        loginPage.login("admin", "admin123");
        Assert.assertTrue(driver.getCurrentUrl().contains("dashboard"));
    }

    @Test
    public void verifyInvalidLogin() {
        loginPage.login("wrong", "wrong");
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.isErrorDisplayed());
    }
}

// Multilevel example
public class SmokeTestSuite extends BaseTest {
    // smoke-specific helpers
}

public class CriticalPathTest extends SmokeTestSuite {
    // inherits from SmokeTest which inherits from BaseTest
}

Method Overriding

public class Animal {
    public void makeSound() {
        System.out.println("Some sound");
    }
}

public class Dog extends Animal {
    @Override  // runtime polymorphism
    public void makeSound() {
        System.out.println("Bark");
    }
}

// Automation example
public class BasePage {
    public void waitForPageLoad() {
        new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(30))
            .until(d -> ((JavascriptExecutor) d)
                .executeScript("return document.readyState").equals("complete"));
    }
}

public class AngularPage extends BasePage {
    @Override
    public void waitForPageLoad() {
        super.waitForPageLoad();  // call parent first
        // additional wait for Angular app to stabilize
        new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(15))
            .until(d -> (Boolean) ((JavascriptExecutor) d)
                .executeScript("return window.getAllAngularTestabilities().length > 0"));
    }
}

super Keyword

Refers to immediate parent class. Used to call parent constructor (super()), access parent fields (super.driver), or invoke overridden parent methods (super.waitForPageLoad()).

Why Multiple Inheritance Not Supported — Diamond Problem

        ClassA
       /      \
   method()  method()
     /          \
 ClassB        ClassC
     \          /
      \        /
       ClassD  ← Which method() does D inherit?

If ClassB and ClassC both override method() differently, ClassD inheriting from both creates ambiguity. Java avoids this by allowing single class inheritance + multiple interface implementation.

Selenium Usage

BaseTest provides driver setup/teardown. All test classes extend it — DRY principle. Common waits, screenshots, and reporting live in the base class.

Polymorphism

Definition

"Many forms" — same interface, different implementations. Enables flexible, extensible code.

Compile-Time Polymorphism (Method Overloading)

Same method name, different parameter lists. Resolved at compile time.

public class ElementHelper {
    // Overloaded click methods
    public void click(By locator) {
        driver.findElement(locator).click();
    }

    public void click(WebElement element) {
        element.click();
    }

    public void click(By locator, int timeoutSeconds) {
        new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(timeoutSeconds))
            .until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator)).click();
    }
}

// Usage — compiler picks method based on arguments
helper.click(By.id("submit"));                    // By version
helper.click(driver.findElement(By.id("submit"))); // WebElement version
helper.click(By.id("submit"), 20);                 // By + timeout version

Runtime Polymorphism (Method Overriding)

Parent reference holds child object. Method invoked depends on actual object type at runtime.

// THE most important polymorphism in Selenium:
WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();   // parent ref → child object
driver = new FirefoxDriver();            // same ref, different implementation
driver = new EdgeDriver();               // swap at runtime

driver.get("https://example.com");       // each browser executes its own get()

// Another example
BaseTest test = new LoginTest();  // reference type BaseTest, actual object LoginTest
test.setUp();                     // calls LoginTest's setUp if overridden

// Interface polymorphism
List<WebElement> elements = driver.findElements(By.tagName("a"));
// ArrayList or other implementation returned — you use List interface

Real-World Analogy

A "Remote Control" button (interface) works on any TV brand (implementation). Press "volume up" — Samsung or LG each handle it their way.

Interview Q&A — Polymorphism

Q: Give a runtime polymorphism example from your framework.
A: WebDriver driver = DriverFactory.getDriver(browser); — factory returns ChromeDriver, FirefoxDriver, or EdgeDriver based on config, but all tests use the WebDriver interface.

Abstraction

Definition

Abstraction hides complex implementation details and exposes only essential features. Achieved via abstract classes and interfaces.

Real-World Analogy

Driving a car — you use steering wheel and pedals (interface) without understanding fuel injection internals (implementation).

Abstract Class Example

public abstract class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;

    public BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(15));
    }

    // Abstract method — must be implemented by subclasses
    public abstract boolean isPageLoaded();

    // Concrete method — shared implementation
    public String getPageTitle() {
        return driver.getTitle();
    }

    protected void click(By locator) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator)).click();
    }
}

public class HomePage extends BasePage {
    private By logo = By.id("logo");

    public HomePage(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
    }

    @Override
    public boolean isPageLoaded() {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(logo)).isDisplayed();
    }
}

Interface Example

public interface Retryable {
    int MAX_RETRIES = 3;  // public static final by default

    boolean execute();     // public abstract by default

    default void onFailure(int attempt) {  // Java 8+ default method
        System.out.println("Attempt " + attempt + " failed, retrying...");
    }
}

public class FlakyElementClick implements Retryable {
    private WebDriver driver;
    private By locator;

    public FlakyElementClick(WebDriver driver, By locator) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.locator = locator;
    }

    @Override
    public boolean execute() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= MAX_RETRIES; i++) {
            try {
                driver.findElement(locator).click();
                return true;
            } catch (ElementClickInterceptedException e) {
                onFailure(i);
            }
        }
        return false;
    }
}

Selenium: WebDriver Interface

// WebDriver is an interface; ChromeDriver implements it
WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();
// You program to the interface, not the implementation
// Enables browser-agnostic test code

Abstract Class vs Interface

AspectAbstract ClassInterface
InstantiationCannot instantiateCannot instantiate
MethodsAbstract + concrete methodsAbstract (implicit), default, static methods (Java 8+)
FieldsAny access modifierpublic static final only
InheritanceSingle class extendsMultiple interfaces implement
ConstructorYesNo
When to useShared state/implementation (BasePage)Contract/capability (Retryable, Searchable)
ExampleBasePage with common wait logicWebDriver, TakesScreenshot

Constructor

Types & Chaining

public class TestData {
    private String username;
    private String password;
    private String environment;

    // Default constructor
    public TestData() {
        this("defaultUser", "defaultPass", "qa");  // constructor chaining via this()
    }

    // Parameterized
    public TestData(String username, String password, String environment) {
        this.username = username;
        this.password = password;
        this.environment = environment;
    }

    // Copy constructor
    public TestData(TestData other) {
        this(other.username, other.password, other.environment);
    }
}

public class AdminTestData extends TestData {
    public AdminTestData() {
        super("admin", "admin123", "staging");  // super() calls parent constructor
    }
}
  • Constructor chaining — this() calls another constructor in same class; must be first statement
  • super() — calls parent constructor; must be first statement if used
  • If no constructor defined, JVM provides default no-arg constructor

HAS-AComposition/AggregationClass contains another classLoginPage has WebDriverPage Object HAS-A driver reference
AssociationUsesTwo classes related, independent lifecyclesTest uses Helper classTest class uses ReportGenerator
AggregationWeak HAS-AWhole has parts; parts can exist independentlyTestSuite has TestsSuite contains tests that run standalone
CompositionStrong HAS-APart cannot exist without wholeCar has EnginePage Object composes WebDriverWait tied to its driver

Interview Q&A — Section 2 (20+ Questions)

Q1: What are the four pillars of OOP?

A: Encapsulation, Inheritance, Polymorphism, Abstraction.

Q2: Difference between method overloading and overriding?

A: Overloading: same class, same name, different params, compile-time. Overriding: parent-child, same signature, runtime dispatch based on object type.

Q3: Can you override static methods?

A: No — static methods belong to the class, not instance. Subclass can define same signature (method hiding), but it's not true overriding. No dynamic dispatch.

Q4: Can you override private methods?

A: No — private methods are not visible to subclasses. Subclass can define same signature but it's a new method, not an override.

Q5: Why use Page Object Model?

A: Encapsulates locators and actions (encapsulation), enables reuse via inheritance (BasePage), supports polymorphism (different page implementations), and abstracts UI complexity from test logic.

Q6: IS-A vs HAS-A — which is LoginPage and WebDriver?

A: LoginPage HAS-A WebDriver (composition/association). LoginTest IS-A BaseTest (inheritance).

Q7: When to use abstract class vs interface?

A: Abstract class when subclasses share state and common implementation (BasePage). Interface when defining a contract multiple unrelated classes implement (Retryable, WebDriver).

Q8: Can an abstract class have a constructor?

A: Yes. Called when subclass object is created via super(). Initializes abstract class fields.

Q9: Can an interface extend another interface?

A: Yes. Interface inheritance is supported: interface B extends A.

Q10: What is the Diamond Problem?

A: Ambiguity when a class inherits two classes with same method. Java prevents multiple class inheritance. Interfaces with default methods require explicit override if both define same method.

Q11: What is composition over inheritance?

A: Design principle: prefer HAS-A (composition) over IS-A (inheritance) for flexibility. Example: inject WebDriverHelper into Page instead of extending it — easier to test and swap.

Q12: Explain @Override annotation.

A: Tells compiler to verify method actually overrides a parent method. Catches typos in method signatures at compile time.

Q13: Can a constructor be private?

A: Yes — Singleton pattern, utility classes (ConfigReader). Prevents external instantiation.

Q14: What is final keyword in OOP context?

A: final class — cannot extend. final method — cannot override. final variable — cannot reassign (constant reference).

Q15: Runtime polymorphism example with collections?

A: List<String> data = new ArrayList<>(); — reference is List, implementation is ArrayList. Methods like add(), get() dispatch to ArrayList at runtime.

Q16: How does WebDriver demonstrate abstraction?

A: WebDriver interface defines get(), findElement(), quit() without browser-specific code. ChromeDriver, FirefoxDriver provide implementations hidden from test code.

Q17: Can you instantiate an abstract class?

A: No. Must create concrete subclass that implements all abstract methods.

Q18: Difference between aggregation and composition?

A: Aggregation: weak ownership, parts survive independently (TestSuite ↔ Tests). Composition: strong ownership, parts destroyed with whole (Order ↔ OrderItems).

Q19: Why is BaseTest usually abstract?

A: Provides shared setup/teardown but isn't a test itself. Abstract prevents accidental instantiation while forcing subclasses to implement test methods.

Q20: How do default interface methods affect multiple inheritance?

A: A class implementing two interfaces with conflicting default methods must override and specify which to use: InterfaceA.super.method().

Q21: What is coupling and how does OOP reduce it?

A: Coupling = dependency between classes. Encapsulation and interfaces reduce coupling — tests depend on Page Object public methods, not internal locators or WebDriver details.

Q22: Explain Object class role in inheritance.

A: Every class implicitly extends java.lang.Object. Inherits equals(), hashCode(), toString(), getClass(). Override toString() in Page Objects for meaningful debug output.

Section 3: Variables & Data Types

Primitive Data Types

TypeSizeRangeDefaultExample
byte1 byte (8 bit)-128 to 1270byte retryCount = 3;
short2 bytes-32,768 to 32,7670short port = 8080;
int4 bytes-2³¹ to 2³¹-10int timeout = 30;
long8 bytes-2⁶³ to 2⁶³-10Llong timestamp = 1710000000L;
float4 bytes~±3.4E+38 (6-7 digits)0.0ffloat price = 19.99f;
double8 bytes~±1.7E+308 (15 digits)0.0ddouble responseTime = 1.234;
char2 bytes (Unicode)'\u0000' to '\uffff''\u0000'char grade = 'A';
boolean1 bit (JVM dependent)true / falsefalseboolean isDisplayed = true;

Non-Primitive (Reference) Types

  • String — sequence of characters; immutable; most used in assertions
  • Array — fixed-size collection of same type: String[] browsers = {"chrome", "firefox"};
  • Class — custom types: WebDriver, LoginPage
  • Interface — contract types: List<WebElement>, Map<String, String>

Variable Types

Local Variables

Declared inside methods, constructors, or blocks. No default value — must initialize before use. Scope limited to the block.

public void validateRowCount() {
    int rowCount = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table/tbody/tr")).size();
    boolean isValid = rowCount > 0;  // must initialize
    Assert.assertTrue(isValid);
    // rowCount destroyed when method ends (stack)
}

Instance Variables

Declared inside class, outside methods. Each object gets its own copy. Default values assigned (0, false, null).

public class SearchResultsPage {
    private WebDriver driver;       // null until constructor runs
    private int resultCount = 0;    // per-object state
    private String lastQuery;       // null default

    public int getResultCount() {
        return resultCount;  // instance variable accessible in all instance methods
    }
}

Static (Class) Variables

Shared across all instances. One copy in memory. Belong to the class, not any object. Access via class name.

public class TestConfig {
    public static String BASE_URL = "https://qa.example.com";
    public static int DEFAULT_TIMEOUT = 15;
    private static int testRunCount = 0;

    public static void incrementRunCount() {
        testRunCount++;  // shared across all tests
    }
}

// Usage — no object needed
driver.get(TestConfig.BASE_URL);

Type Casting

Widening (Implicit) — Safe, Automatic

Smaller type → larger type. No data loss.

int timeout = 10;
long longTimeout = timeout;     // int → long (implicit)
double precise = timeout;       // int → double (implicit)

byte small = 5;
int larger = small;               // byte → int → automatic

Narrowing (Explicit) — Requires Cast, Possible Data Loss

double responseTime = 1234.567;
int rounded = (int) responseTime;  // 1234 — decimal lost

long big = 9999999999L;
int smaller = (int) big;           // overflow possible

// Selenium — casting WebDriver to JavascriptExecutor
WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();
JavascriptExecutor js = (JavascriptExecutor) driver;  // explicit cast
js.executeScript("window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight)");

Autoboxing & Unboxing

Automatic conversion between primitives and wrapper classes (Java 5+).

PrimitiveWrapper ClassExample
byteByteByte b = 10; (autoboxing)
shortShortshort s = new Short((short)5); (unboxing)
intIntegerInteger count = elements.size();
longLongLong id = 123456789L;
floatFloatFloat rate = 3.14f;
doubleDoubleDouble avg = calculateAverage();
charCharacterCharacter ch = 'X';
booleanBooleanBoolean visible = element.isDisplayed();
 
// Autoboxing: primitive → wrapper
int primitiveCount = 5;
Integer wrapperCount = primitiveCount;  // auto

// Unboxing: wrapper → primitive
Integer size = driver.findElements(By.tagName("li")).size();
int listSize = size;  // auto unboxing

// NullPointerException risk on unboxing!
Integer nullInt = null;
// int bad = nullInt;  // NPE at runtime!

var Keyword (Java 10+)

Local variable type inference. Compiler deduces type from initializer. Cannot use for fields or method params.

var driver = new ChromeDriver();                    // inferred: ChromeDriver
var elements = driver.findElements(By.tagName("a")); // inferred: List<WebElement>
var title = driver.getTitle();                       // inferred: String
var wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10)); // WebDriverWait

// Must initialize — var x; is invalid
// Cannot use when type isn't obvious: var x = null;

Selenium Usage Examples

// Storing element text
String actualTitle = driver.getTitle();
String buttonText = driver.findElement(By.id("submit")).getText();

// Counts
int rowCount = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//tr")).size();
int linkCount = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector("a")).size();

// Boolean checks
boolean isEnabled = driver.findElement(By.id("btn")).isEnabled();
boolean isSelected = driver.findElement(By.id("checkbox")).isSelected();
boolean isDisplayed = driver.findElement(By.id("modal")).isDisplayed();

// Assertions
Assert.assertEquals("Expected Title", actualTitle);
Assert.assertTrue(isEnabled, "Submit button should be enabled");
Assert.assertEquals(10, rowCount, "Table should have 10 rows");

Interview Q&A — Section 3

Q1: How many primitive types does Java have?

A: 8 — byte, short, int, long, float, double, char, boolean.

Q2: Difference between primitive and reference types?

A: Primitives store actual values on stack (when local). References store memory addresses pointing to heap objects. Primitives have default values; references default to null.

Q3: What is the default value of an instance int variable?

A: 0. Local int variables have no default — compiler error if used uninitialized.

Q4: Can static variables be accessed without creating an object?

A: Yes. TestConfig.BASE_URL — belongs to class, not instance.

Q5: What happens if you unbox a null Integer?

A: NullPointerException. Always null-check wrapper types before unboxing.

Q6: Why cast WebDriver to JavascriptExecutor?

A: WebDriver interface doesn't declare executeScript(). JavascriptExecutor extends WebDriver capabilities. Cast is safe when using ChromeDriver/FirefoxDriver which implement both.

Q7: When to use long vs int for timestamps?

A: System.currentTimeMillis() returns long — exceeds int range. Always use long for timestamps and large counts.

Q8: What is var and its limitations?

A: Local type inference (Java 10+). Only for local variables with initializer. Not for fields, method parameters, or return types. Improves readability for complex generics.

Q9: Difference between float and double?

A: double has double precision (8 bytes, ~15 digits). float has single precision (4 bytes, ~6 digits). Use double by default; float only when memory-critical.

Q10: Can boolean be converted to int?

A: No implicit conversion. Use ternary: int val = flag ? 1 : 0; Unlike C/C++.

Q11: What is scope of a local variable?

A: From declaration to end of block (method, loop, if-block). Cannot access outside declaring block.

Q12: Why use Integer instead of int in collections?

A: Generics don't support primitives. List<Integer> not List<int>. Autoboxing handles conversion transparently.

Section 4: Operators & Control Statements

Operators

Arithmetic Operators

OperatorSyntaxExampleAutomation Use
+a + btotal = passed + failed;Concatenate strings: "Test " + testId
-a - bremaining = max - current;Calculate retry attempts left
*a * bdelay = seconds * 1000;Convert seconds to milliseconds
/a / bavg = total / count;Average response time
%a % bretry % 3 == 0Cycle through test data sets

Relational Operators

int actualCount = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//tr")).size();
int expectedCount = 10;

boolean isEqual       = (actualCount == expectedCount);
boolean isNotEqual    = (actualCount != expectedCount);
boolean isLess        = (actualCount < expectedCount);
boolean isGreater     = (actualCount > expectedCount);
boolean isLessOrEqual = (actualCount <= expectedCount);

Logical Operators

WebElement btn = driver.findElement(By.id("submit"));
boolean canClick = btn.isDisplayed() && btn.isEnabled();
boolean shouldSkip = btn.isDisplayed() || btn.isEnabled();
boolean isHidden   = !btn.isDisplayed();

// Short-circuit: && stops if first is false; || stops if first is true
if (driver != null && driver.getTitle().contains("Login")) { /* safe */ }

Assignment Operators

int retryCount = 0;
retryCount += 1;    // retryCount = retryCount + 1
retryCount -= 1;
timeout *= 2;       // double the timeout
index /= 2;

Ternary Operator

String browser = System.getProperty("browser", "chrome");
String driverPath = browser.equals("chrome")
    ? "drivers/chromedriver.exe"
    : "drivers/geckodriver.exe";

String status = testPassed ? "PASS" : "FAIL";
int timeout = isProd ? 30 : 10;

instanceof Operator

WebDriver driver = DriverFactory.getDriver("chrome");

if (driver instanceof ChromeDriver) {
    ChromeOptions options = new ChromeOptions();
    // Chrome-specific setup
}

if (driver instanceof TakesScreenshot) {
    TakesScreenshot ts = (TakesScreenshot) driver;
    File screenshot = ts.getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
}

if (driver instanceof JavascriptExecutor) {
    ((JavascriptExecutor) driver).executeScript("alert('test')");
}

Control Statements

if / else if / else

WebElement errorMsg = driver.findElement(By.id("error"));

if (errorMsg.isDisplayed()) {
    Assert.fail("Login failed: " + errorMsg.getText());
} else if (driver.getCurrentUrl().contains("dashboard")) {
    System.out.println("Login successful");
} else {
    Assert.fail("Unexpected state after login");
}

// Check element visibility before interaction
WebElement modal = driver.findElement(By.id("popup"));
if (modal.isDisplayed()) {
    driver.findElement(By.id("closeModal")).click();
}

switch Statement

// Browser selection factory
String browser = ConfigReader.getProperty("browser");
WebDriver driver;

switch (browser.toLowerCase()) {
    case "chrome":
        driver = new ChromeDriver();
        break;
    case "firefox":
        driver = new FirefoxDriver();
        break;
    case "edge":
        driver = new EdgeDriver();
        break;
    default:
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unsupported browser: " + browser);
}

// Environment selection (Java 14+ switch expression)
String env = ConfigReader.getProperty("env");
String baseUrl = switch (env) {
    case "dev"  -> "https://dev.example.com";
    case "qa"   -> "https://qa.example.com";
    case "prod" -> "https://www.example.com";
    default     -> throw new InvalidConfigException("Unknown env: " + env);
};

for Loop — Iterate Elements

List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table/tbody/tr"));
for (int i = 0; i < rows.size(); i++) {
    String cellText = rows.get(i).findElement(By.tagName("td")).getText();
    System.out.println("Row " + i + ": " + cellText);
}

Enhanced for Loop

List<WebElement> links = driver.findElements(By.tagName("a"));
for (WebElement link : links) {
    System.out.println(link.getText() + " -> " + link.getAttribute("href"));
}

String[] browsers = {"chrome", "firefox", "edge"};
for (String b : browsers) {
    runTestOnBrowser(b);
}

while Loop — Wait / Retry Logic

// Retry until success or max attempts
int attempts = 0;
int maxRetries = 3;
boolean clicked = false;

while (attempts < maxRetries && !clicked) {
    try {
        driver.findElement(By.id("flakyBtn")).click();
        clicked = true;
    } catch (ElementClickInterceptedException e) {
        attempts++;
        Thread.sleep(1000);
    }
}

// Wait until condition
int waitSeconds = 0;
while (!driver.getTitle().contains("Dashboard") && waitSeconds < 30) {
    Thread.sleep(1000);
    waitSeconds++;
}

do-while Loop — Execute At Least Once

int page = 1;
do {
    navigateToPage(page);
    scrapeData();
    page++;
} while (hasNextPage() && page <= 10);

// Accept alert at least once attempt
do {
    try {
        driver.switchTo().alert().accept();
    } catch (NoAlertPresentException e) {
        break;
    }
} while (true);

break and continue

// break — stop iteration
for (WebElement row : rows) {
    if (row.getText().contains("ERROR")) {
        Assert.fail("Error row found: " + row.getText());
        break;
    }
}

// continue — skip current iteration
for (WebElement link : links) {
    String href = link.getAttribute("href");
    if (href == null || href.isEmpty()) {
        continue;  // skip empty links
    }
    validateLink(href);
}

Automation-Specific Examples

Iterate Dropdown Options

Select dropdown = new Select(driver.findElement(By.id("country")));
List<WebElement> options = dropdown.getOptions();

for (WebElement option : options) {
    String value = option.getAttribute("value");
    dropdown.selectByValue(value);
    Assert.assertTrue(driver.findElement(By.id("result")).isDisplayed());
}

Count Table Rows

int dataRows = 0;
List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table[@id='data']/tbody/tr"));

for (WebElement row : rows) {
    if (!row.getAttribute("class").contains("hidden")) {
        dataRows++;
    }
}
Assert.assertEquals(25, dataRows, "Expected 25 visible data rows");

Conditional Test Execution

String runEnv = System.getProperty("env", "qa");

if ("prod".equals(runEnv)) {
    throw new SkipException("Smoke tests only on prod — skipping data mutation tests");
}

if (ConfigReader.getProperty("feature.newUI").equals("true")) {
    runNewUITestSuite();
} else {
    runLegacyUITestSuite();
}

Browser Factory Switch

public class DriverFactory {
    public static WebDriver createDriver(String browser) {
        return switch (browser.toLowerCase()) {
            case "chrome"  -> new ChromeDriver(getChromeOptions());
            case "firefox" -> new FirefoxDriver(getFirefoxOptions());
            case "edge"    -> new EdgeDriver(getEdgeOptions());
            case "remote"  -> new RemoteWebDriver(getGridUrl(), getChromeOptions());
            default -> throw new IllegalArgumentException("Browser not supported: " + browser);
        };
    }
}

Interview Q&A — Section 4

Q1: Difference between == and .equals() for Strings?

A: == compares references (memory addresses). .equals() compares content. Always use .equals() for String value comparison in assertions.

Q2: When to use switch vs if-else?

A: switch for discrete values of one variable (browser, env). if-else for complex boolean conditions (element visible AND enabled).

Q3: What is short-circuit evaluation?

A: && doesn't evaluate second operand if first is false. || skips second if first is true. Prevents NPE: if (driver != null && driver.getTitle().equals("X")).

Q4: Can switch work with String?

A: Yes, since Java 7. Common in browser/env selection. Use .toLowerCase() for case-insensitive matching.

Q5: Difference between while and do-while?

A: while checks condition first (may never execute). do-while executes at least once, then checks. Use do-while when first attempt must always run.

Q6: How does instanceof help in frameworks?

A: Safely check capabilities before casting — TakesScreenshot for screenshots, JavascriptExecutor for JS clicks, RemoteWebDriver for Grid sessions.

Q7: What is break vs continue?

A: break exits the loop entirely. continue skips remaining code in current iteration and moves to next. break in nested loops only exits innermost loop unless labeled.

Q8: Can you use String in switch with null?

A: No — NullPointerException if switch variable is null. Null-check before switch.

Q9: Enhanced for vs traditional for?

A: Enhanced for is cleaner, read-only (no index modification), works with arrays and Iterable. Traditional for needed when you need index or modify list during iteration.

Q10: What is ternary operator advantage?

A: Concise conditional assignment. Useful for inline config: timeout values, driver paths, pass/fail status strings.

Q11: How to iterate Map in automation?

A: for (Map.Entry<String, String> entry : configMap.entrySet()) or keySet()/values() with enhanced for.

Q12: What happens with missing break in switch?

A: Fall-through — execution continues into next case. Sometimes intentional, usually a bug. Use break or switch expressions (Java 14+) to prevent.

Section 5: Strings

String — Immutable

Once created, a String object cannot be modified. Any "modification" creates a new String object on the heap. This ensures thread safety and enables the String pool optimization.

String Pool Concept

  HEAP                              STRING POOL (inside Heap)
 ┌─────────────────────┐            ┌──────────────────────────┐
 │ String s1 = new     │            │  "Hello"  ◄── s3         │
 │   String("Hello")   │──┐         │  "World"  ◄── s4, s5     │
 │  (new object)       │  │         │  (shared literals)       │
 └─────────────────────┘  │         └──────────────────────────┘
                          │
 ┌─────────────────────┐  │         s3 = "Hello"  → checks pool, reuses
 │ String s2 = new     │──┘         s4 = "World"
 │   String("Hello")   │            s5 = "World"  → same reference as s4
 │  (another new obj)  │
 └─────────────────────┘

  s1 == s2  → false  (different heap objects)
  s3 == s4  → false  (different literals)
  s4 == s5  → true   (same pool reference)
  s1.equals(s2) → true (same content)

== vs .equals()

String a = "Selenium";
String b = "Selenium";
String c = new String("Selenium");

System.out.println(a == b);       // true  — same pool reference
System.out.println(a == c);       // false — different objects
System.out.println(a.equals(c));  // true  — same content ✓ USE THIS

// In assertions — ALWAYS use equals
Assert.assertEquals("Login Successful", actualMessage);
Assert.assertTrue(actualUrl.contains("/dashboard"));

StringBuilder vs StringBuffer

AspectStringStringBuilderStringBuffer
MutabilityImmutableMutableMutable
Thread-safeYes (immutable)NoYes (synchronized)
PerformanceSlow for concatenation in loopsFastSlower than StringBuilder
StorageString Pool + HeapHeap onlyHeap only
When to useConstants, assertions, paramsBuilding strings in loops (reports)Multi-threaded string building
IntroducedJava 1.0Java 5Java 1.0
 
// BAD — creates many String objects in loop
String report = "";
for (String result : testResults) {
    report = report + result + "\n";  // new String each iteration
}

// GOOD — StringBuilder
StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
for (String result : testResults) {
    sb.append(result).append("\n");
}
String report = sb.toString();

Important String Methods

equals() / equalsIgnoreCase()

String actual = driver.findElement(By.id("msg")).getText();
Assert.assertEquals("Success", actual);                    // TestNG uses equals internally
Assert.assertTrue(actual.equalsIgnoreCase("SUCCESS"));     // case-insensitive

contains()

String url = driver.getCurrentUrl();
Assert.assertTrue(url.contains("/dashboard"), "Should be on dashboard");
Assert.assertTrue(errorMsg.contains("invalid credentials"));

startsWith() / endsWith()

String currentUrl = driver.getCurrentUrl();
Assert.assertTrue(currentUrl.startsWith("https://"), "Must be HTTPS");
Assert.assertTrue(currentUrl.endsWith("/login") || currentUrl.contains("/login"));

replace() / replaceAll()

String raw = "test@email.com;admin@email.com";
String cleaned = raw.replace(";", ",");           // literal replace
String digits = "Order #12345".replaceAll("[^0-9]", "");  // regex: "12345"
String locator = "xpath=//div[@id='btn']".replace("xpath=", "");

split()

// Parse CSV test data
String csvLine = "admin,password123,QA";
String[] credentials = csvLine.split(",");
String username = credentials[0];  // "admin"
String password = credentials[1];  // "password123"

// Split URL path
String[] pathParts = driver.getCurrentUrl().split("/");
String pageName = pathParts[pathParts.length - 1];

substring()

String orderId = "Order ID: ORD-98765";
String id = orderId.substring(10);       // "ORD-98765"
String prefix = orderId.substring(0, 9); // "Order ID:"

String date = "2024-03-15";
String year = date.substring(0, 4);      // "2024"

trim() / strip() (Java 11+)

String input = "  admin  ";
String clean = input.trim();   // "admin" — removes leading/trailing whitespace
String clean2 = input.strip(); // Unicode-aware whitespace removal

String text = driver.findElement(By.id("label")).getText().strip();

length()

String password = "abc";
Assert.assertTrue(password.length() >= 8, "Password must be at least 8 chars");

String searchResults = driver.findElement(By.id("count")).getText();
// "Showing 42 results"
int count = Integer.parseInt(searchResults.replaceAll("[^0-9]", ""));

toLowerCase() / toUpperCase()

String browser = System.getProperty("browser", "chrome").toLowerCase();
String status = testResult.toUpperCase();  // "PASS"

Assert.assertEquals("LOGIN PAGE",
    driver.findElement(By.tagName("h1")).getText().toUpperCase());

charAt() / indexOf()

String text = "Error: Element not found";
int colonIndex = text.indexOf(":");           // 5
char firstChar = text.charAt(0);              // 'E'
int notFound = text.indexOf("not found");     // 16
int lastIndex = text.lastIndexOf("e");        // 20

matches()

String email = "user@example.com";
Assert.assertTrue(email.matches("^[\\w.-]+@[\\w.-]+\\.[a-zA-Z]{2,}$"));

String price = driver.findElement(By.className("price")).getText();
Assert.assertTrue(price.matches("\\$\\d+\\.\\d{2}"));  // "$19.99"

format()

String testName = "LoginTest";
String message = String.format("Test [%s] %s in %d ms", testName, "PASSED", 1234);
// "Test [LoginTest] PASSED in 1234 ms"

String locator = String.format("//button[@id='%s']", buttonId);
String url = String.format("%s/users/%d/profile", baseUrl, userId);

String Immutability — Interview Deep-Dive

String s = "Hello";
s.concat(" World");    // returns NEW String "Hello World" — s still "Hello"
s = s.concat(" World"); // s now references new object

// Why immutable?
// 1. String Pool — safe sharing without synchronization
// 2. Security — params, URLs, class names can't be tampered
// 3. Thread safety — no sync needed for read-only strings
// 4. HashCode caching — hashCode computed once, cached

// String concatenation at compile time is optimized:
String x = "Hello" + " " + "World";  // compiler creates "Hello World" in pool

// Loop concatenation is NOT optimized — use StringBuilder

Selenium String Usage

// getText() — visible text of element
String heading = driver.findElement(By.tagName("h1")).getText();

// getAttribute() — HTML attribute value
String href = link.getAttribute("href");
String value = input.getAttribute("value");
String className = element.getAttribute("class");

// URL manipulation
String currentUrl = driver.getCurrentUrl();
String baseUrl = currentUrl.split("/")[2];  // extract domain
driver.get(baseUrl + "/logout");

10 Coding Questions with Solutions

Q1: Reverse a string without StringBuilder.reverse()

public static String reverse(String input) {
    char[] chars = input.toCharArray();
    int left = 0, right = chars.length - 1;
    while (left < right) {
        char temp = chars[left];
        chars[left++] = chars[right];
        chars[right--] = temp;
    }
    return new String(chars);
}

Q2: Check if two strings are anagrams

public static boolean isAnagram(String s1, String s2) {
    if (s1.length() != s2.length()) return false;
    char[] a = s1.toLowerCase().toCharArray();
    char[] b = s2.toLowerCase().toCharArray();
    Arrays.sort(a);
    Arrays.sort(b);
    return Arrays.equals(a, b);
}

Q3: Count vowels in a string

public static int countVowels(String s) {
    int count = 0;
    for (char c : s.toLowerCase().toCharArray()) {
        if ("aeiou".indexOf(c) >= 0) count++;
    }
    return count;
}

Q4: Remove duplicates from string

public static String removeDuplicates(String s) {
    StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
    for (char c : s.toCharArray()) {
        if (sb.indexOf(String.valueOf(c)) == -1) {
            sb.append(c);
        }
    }
    return sb.toString();
}

Q5: Check palindrome

public static boolean isPalindrome(String s) {
    String cleaned = s.replaceAll("[^a-zA-Z0-9]", "").toLowerCase();
    return cleaned.equals(new StringBuilder(cleaned).reverse().toString());
}

Q6: Find first non-repeating character

public static char firstNonRepeating(String s) {
    Map<Character, Integer> freq = new LinkedHashMap<>();
    for (char c : s.toCharArray()) {
        freq.merge(c, 1, Integer::sum);
    }
    return freq.entrySet().stream()
        .filter(e -> e.getValue() == 1)
        .map(Map.Entry::getKey)
        .findFirst().orElse('_');
}

Q7: Convert String to int without parseInt

public static int stringToInt(String s) {
    int result = 0;
    for (char c : s.toCharArray()) {
        result = result * 10 + (c - '0');
    }
    return result;
}

Q8: Extract numbers from string

public static String extractNumbers(String s) {
    return s.replaceAll("[^0-9]", "");
}
// "Price: $49.99" → "4999"

Q9: Capitalize first letter of each word

public static String capitalizeWords(String s) {
    String[] words = s.split("\\s+");
    StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
    for (String word : words) {
        if (!word.isEmpty()) {
            sb.append(Character.toUpperCase(word.charAt(0)))
              .append(word.substring(1).toLowerCase()).append(" ");
        }
    }
    return sb.toString().strip();
}

Q10: Compare version strings "1.10.2" vs "1.9.0"

public static int compareVersions(String v1, String v2) {
    String[] parts1 = v1.split("\\.");
    String[] parts2 = v2.split("\\.");
    int len = Math.max(parts1.length, parts2.length);
    for (int i = 0; i < len; i++) {
        int n1 = i < parts1.length ? Integer.parseInt(parts1[i]) : 0;
        int n2 = i < parts2.length ? Integer.parseInt(parts2[i]) : 0;
        if (n1 != n2) return Integer.compare(n1, n2);
    }
    return 0;
}

Interview Q&A — Section 5

Q1: Why is String immutable?

A: Security (class loading, network connections), thread safety, String pool optimization, and hashCode caching. Immutable objects are inherently thread-safe.

Q2: How many objects created: String s = new String("Hello");?

A: Potentially 2 — "Hello" in pool (if not already) + new heap object from new keyword.

Q3: String vs StringBuilder performance in loops?

A: String concatenation in loop creates O(n²) objects. StringBuilder creates O(n) — always use StringBuilder for dynamic string building.

Q4: Is String thread-safe?

A: Yes — immutability guarantees thread safety. StringBuffer is mutable but synchronized. StringBuilder is mutable and not thread-safe.

Q5: What is String.intern()?

A: Moves String to pool and returns pool reference. s.intern() — rarely needed in automation; useful for memory optimization with many duplicate strings.

Q6: replace() vs replaceAll()?

A: replace() takes CharSequence literals. replaceAll() takes regex patterns. replaceAll("[0-9]", "") removes all digits.

Q7: How to compare strings ignoring whitespace?

A: s1.strip().equals(s2.strip()) or normalize both before comparison.

Q8: What happens with String concatenation and null?

A: "Hello " + null produces "Hello null" (null converted to "null" string). But null.equals("x") throws NPE — always put literal first: "x".equals(variable).

Q9: charAt() vs indexOf()?

A: charAt(i) returns char at index i (throws IndexOutOfBounds). indexOf(c) returns first index of char/substring (-1 if not found).

Q10: How to validate email in test assertions?

A: email.matches("^[\\w.-]+@[\\w.-]+\\.[a-zA-Z]{2,}$") or Apache Commons Validator for production frameworks.

Q11: String pool location in Java 7+?

A: Moved from PermGen to Heap. Reduces PermGen OOM issues. Pool still deduplicates string literals.

Q12: Difference between strip() and trim()?

A: trim() removes chars ≤ U+0020 (ASCII whitespace). strip() (Java 11) removes all Unicode whitespace including non-breaking spaces — preferred for modern apps.

Section 6: Arrays & Collections

Arrays

Declaration & Initialization

// 1D Array
String[] browsers = new String[3];           // declare, default null
browsers[0] = "chrome";
browsers[1] = "firefox";
browsers[2] = "edge";

String[] envs = {"dev", "qa", "staging", "prod"};  // literal init
int[] timeouts = new int[]{5, 10, 15, 30};

// 2D Array
String[][] testData = {
    {"admin", "pass123", "QA"},
    {"user1", "userpass", "Dev"},
    {"guest", "guest", "Staging"}
};
String username = testData[0][0];  // "admin"

Array Iteration

// Traditional for
for (int i = 0; i < browsers.length; i++) {
    runTestsOn(browsers[i]);
}

// Enhanced for
for (String browser : browsers) {
    DriverFactory.createDriver(browser);
}

// Streams (Java 8+)
Arrays.stream(browsers).forEach(this::runTestsOn);

Common Operations

int[] nums = {5, 2, 8, 1, 9};
Arrays.sort(nums);                          // [1, 2, 5, 8, 9]
int index = Arrays.binarySearch(nums, 5);   // 2 (must be sorted)
int[] copy = Arrays.copyOf(nums, nums.length);
boolean equal = Arrays.equals(nums, copy);   // true
String str = Arrays.toString(nums);          // "[1, 2, 5, 8, 9]"

Array Limitations → Why Collections?

  • Fixed size — cannot grow/shrink dynamically
  • No built-in methods for add, remove, search (manual implementation)
  • Cannot store heterogeneous types (without Object[])
  • No ready-made Set (unique) or Map (key-value) semantics
  • Collections provide ArrayList, HashSet, HashMap with rich APIs

Collections Framework Hierarchy

                    Iterable
                       │
                   Collection
                  /    |    \
               List   Set   Queue
                │      │      │
           ArrayList  HashSet  PriorityQueue
           LinkedList LinkedHashSet  Deque
                    TreeSet    │
                              ArrayDeque
                              LinkedList

        Map (separate hierarchy — not a Collection)
         │
    HashMap ─── LinkedHashMap ─── TreeMap
    Hashtable (legacy, synchronized)
    ConcurrentHashMap (thread-safe)

List Interface

ArrayList — Internal Working

Dynamic array internally. Default capacity 10. When full, grows by ~50% (newCapacity = old + old/2). Fast random access O(1). Slow middle insert/delete O(n) due to shifting.

List<WebElement> elements = new ArrayList<>();
elements.add(driver.findElement(By.id("btn1")));
elements.add(driver.findElement(By.id("btn2")));
WebElement first = elements.get(0);  // O(1) access

List<String> testData = new ArrayList<>();
testData.add("user1@test.com");
testData.add("user2@test.com");

When to use: Random access, iteration, storing WebElements, test data lists, when size changes frequently.

LinkedList — Doubly Linked List

Each node stores data + prev/next references. O(1) insert/delete at head/tail. O(n) random access. Implements both List and Deque.

LinkedList<String> executionLog = new LinkedList<>();
executionLog.addFirst("Test started");
executionLog.addLast("Login completed");
executionLog.removeFirst();

When to use: Frequent insertions/deletions at beginning/end, queue-like operations. Rare in typical Selenium frameworks.

ArrayList vs LinkedList

AspectArrayListLinkedList
Internal structureDynamic arrayDoubly linked list
Random access (get)O(1) — fastO(n) — slow
Insert at endO(1) amortizedO(1)
Insert/delete middleO(n) — shift elementsO(n) — find + O(1) link
MemoryLess overheadMore (node pointers)
Thread-safeNo (use Collections.synchronizedList)No
Cache performanceBetter (contiguous memory)Poorer (scattered nodes)
Best for automationWebElements, test data, locatorsExecution logs, undo stacks

Set Interface

HashSet

Hash table backing. No duplicates. No order guaranteed. O(1) add/remove/contains. Allows one null.

Set<String> uniqueUrls = new HashSet<>();
uniqueUrls.add("https://example.com/page1");
uniqueUrls.add("https://example.com/page1");  // duplicate ignored
System.out.println(uniqueUrls.size());  // 1

LinkedHashSet

HashSet + doubly-linked list for insertion order preservation.

Set<String> orderedUrls = new LinkedHashSet<>();
orderedUrls.add("/home");
orderedUrls.add("/login");
orderedUrls.add("/dashboard");
// Iteration order: /home, /login, /dashboard

TreeSet

Red-black tree. Sorted order (natural or Comparator). O(log n) operations. No null allowed.

Set<Integer> sortedPriorities = new TreeSet<>();
sortedPriorities.add(3);
sortedPriorities.add(1);
sortedPriorities.add(2);
// Iteration: 1, 2, 3

Set Comparison

AspectHashSetLinkedHashSetTreeSet
OrderingNoneInsertion orderSorted (natural/Comparator)
PerformanceO(1)O(1)O(log n)
Null allowedOne nullOne nullNo
ImplementationHash tableHash table + linked listRed-black tree
Best forUnique test IDs, URLsOrdered unique stepsSorted test priorities
DuplicatesNot allowedNot allowedNot allowed

Map Interface

HashMap — Internal Working

Array of buckets (default 16). hashCode() determines bucket. Collisions handled by linked list (Java 7) or tree (Java 8+, when bucket > 8 nodes). Load factor 0.75 triggers resize (double capacity).

Map<String, String> config = new HashMap<>();
config.put("browser", "chrome");
config.put("base.url", "https://qa.example.com");
config.put("timeout", "15");

String browser = config.get("browser");  // "chrome"
config.getOrDefault("headless", "false");

LinkedHashMap

HashMap + insertion order (or access order if configured).

TreeMap

Sorted by keys. NavigableMap — floorKey, ceilingKey, subMap.

Hashtable (Legacy)

Synchronized, no null keys/values, slower. Replaced by ConcurrentHashMap for thread-safe needs.

HashMap vs Hashtable vs ConcurrentHashMap

AspectHashMapHashtableConcurrentHashMap
Thread-safeNoYes (synchronized methods)Yes (segment/cas locking)
Null keys/valuesOne null key, multiple null valuesNot allowedNot allowed
PerformanceFast (single-threaded)Slow (full lock)Fast (partial locking)
IntroducedJava 1.2Java 1.0 (legacy)Java 1.5
IterationFail-fast iteratorFail-fast enumeratorWeakly consistent
Default forGeneral key-value storageDeprecatedParallel test config sharing
NullPointerExceptionOnly on null key getOn any null key/valueOn any null key/value
Automation useTest params, config mapsProperties class extends itShared state in parallel runs

Queue

// PriorityQueue — natural ordering or Comparator
Queue<Integer> testPriority = new PriorityQueue<>();
testPriority.offer(3);
testPriority.offer(1);
testPriority.poll();  // 1 (lowest first)

// Deque — double-ended queue
Deque<String> browserHistory = new ArrayDeque<>();
browserHistory.push("page1");
browserHistory.push("page2");
browserHistory.pop();  // "page2" — stack behavior

Iterator vs ListIterator vs forEach

List<String> tests = new ArrayList<>(List.of("Login", "Search", "Checkout"));

// Iterator — forward only, works on any Collection
Iterator<String> it = tests.iterator();
while (it.hasNext()) {
    System.out.println(it.next());
    // it.remove(); — safe removal during iteration
}

// ListIterator — bidirectional, List only
ListIterator<String> lit = tests.listIterator();
while (lit.hasNext()) {
    String test = lit.next();
    if (test.equals("Search")) lit.set("SearchV2");  // replace during iteration
}

// forEach (Java 8+) — lambda, cannot modify during iteration
tests.forEach(t -> System.out.println("Running: " + t));

Collections Utility Class

List<Integer> scores = new ArrayList<>(List.of(85, 92, 78, 95, 88));
Collections.sort(scores);                    // [78, 85, 88, 92, 95]
Collections.reverse(scores);                 // [95, 92, 88, 85, 78]
Collections.max(scores);                     // 95
Collections.frequency(scores, 88);           // 1
Collections.shuffle(scores);                 // random order for test data

List<String> immutable = Collections.unmodifiableList(tests);  // prevent modification
List<String> synced = Collections.synchronizedList(tests);   // thread-safe wrapper

Selenium & Framework Usage

// ArrayList — store WebElements
List<WebElement> rows = new ArrayList<>(driver.findElements(By.xpath("//tr")));

// HashMap — test parameters, config
Map<String, String> testParams = new HashMap<>();
testParams.put("username", "admin");
testParams.put("password", "secret");
testParams.put("environment", "qa");

// DataProvider with 2D Object array
@DataProvider(name = "loginData")
public Object[][] getLoginData() {
    Map<String, String> row1 = Map.of("user", "admin", "pass", "admin123");
    Map<String, String> row2 = Map.of("user", "guest", "pass", "guest");
    return new Object[][] {{row1}, {row2}};
}

// Set — unique URLs visited during crawl test
Set<String> visitedUrls = new HashSet<>();

// Properties extends Hashtable
Properties props = new Properties();
props.load(new FileInputStream("config.properties"));
String url = props.getProperty("base.url");

Interview Q&A — Section 6

Q1: Array vs ArrayList?

A: Array: fixed size, primitives allowed, faster. ArrayList: dynamic, objects only (autoboxing), rich API (add, remove, sort). Use ArrayList in automation for flexible test data.

Q2: How does HashMap handle collisions?

A: Same bucket → linked list of entries. Java 8+: when bucket exceeds 8 nodes, converts to red-black tree for O(log n) lookup. Rehashes when load factor exceeds 0.75.

Q3: Why override equals() and hashCode() together?

A: HashMap/HashSet contract: equal objects must have same hashCode. Violating this breaks HashSet deduplication and HashMap lookups.

Q4: ArrayList vs LinkedList for storing WebElements?

A: ArrayList — you iterate and occasionally access by index. LinkedList only if frequent head/tail insertions. ArrayList is default choice.

Q5: HashSet how does it prevent duplicates?

A: Uses hashCode() to find bucket, then equals() to check existing entries. If equals match found, add() returns false.

Q6: ConcurrentHashMap vs Hashtable?

A: ConcurrentHashMap uses finer-grained locking (segments/CAS), much better throughput in parallel tests. Hashtable locks entire table — legacy, avoid.

Q7: Can you add null to HashMap?

A: Yes — one null key, multiple null values. TreeMap and ConcurrentHashMap reject null keys.

Q8: Fail-fast vs fail-safe iterator?

A: Fail-fast (ArrayList, HashMap) throws ConcurrentModificationException if collection modified during iteration (except via iterator.remove()). Fail-safe (ConcurrentHashMap) works on clone, no exception.

Q9: How to sort HashMap by values?

A: Stream API: map.entrySet().stream().sorted(Map.Entry.comparingByValue()).collect(toMap(...)) or TreeMap with custom Comparator.

Q10: What is load factor in HashMap?

A: Default 0.75 — when 75% of buckets are filled, HashMap doubles capacity and rehashes all entries.

Q11: LinkedHashMap use case in automation?

A: Maintaining test step execution order, breadcrumb navigation validation, ordered config loading for reproducible test runs.

Q12: Difference between Collection and Collections?

A: Collection is the root interface. Collections is a utility class with static methods (sort, reverse, synchronized wrappers).

Q13: How to convert List to Array and vice versa?

A: list.toArray(new String[0]) and Arrays.asList(array) or new ArrayList<>(Arrays.asList(array)).

Q14: Why Properties extends Hashtable?

A: Legacy design. Properties is Hashtable<Object, Object> specialized for String key-value config files. Used extensively in config.properties loading.

Q15: TreeSet vs HashSet when to use?

A: HashSet for fast unique collection (test IDs). TreeSet when you need sorted iteration (priority-ordered test cases).

Section 7: Exception Handling

Exception Hierarchy

                        Throwable
                       /         \
                    Error      Exception
                   (JVM-level)     |
                              /         \
                    Checked Exception   RuntimeException
                    (compile-time         (Unchecked)
                     must handle)              |
                    IOException          NullPointerException
                    SQLException         IllegalArgumentException
                    ClassNotFoundException  IndexOutOfBoundsException
                                         NoSuchElementException  ← Selenium
                                         TimeoutException        ← Selenium
                                         StaleElementReferenceException
                                         ElementClickInterceptedException

Checked vs Unchecked Exceptions

AspectCheckedUnchecked (Runtime)
ExtendsException (not RuntimeException)RuntimeException
Compile-time checkMust handle or declare throwsNo compile-time requirement
When thrownRecoverable external failuresProgramming errors, framework failures
ExamplesIOException, SQLExceptionNPE, NoSuchElementException
Handlingtry-catch or throws mandatoryOptional — handle when recoverable
In automationFile not found (test data), networkMost Selenium exceptions

Keywords

try-catch

try {
    driver.findElement(By.id("submit")).click();
} catch (NoSuchElementException e) {
    System.out.println("Element not found: " + e.getMessage());
    takeScreenshot("element_not_found");
    throw e;  // re-throw to fail test
}

// Multiple catch blocks — most specific first
try {
    driver.findElement(By.id("btn")).click();
} catch (ElementClickInterceptedException e) {
    ((JavascriptExecutor) driver).executeScript("arguments[0].click();", element);
} catch (ElementNotInteractableException e) {
    ((JavascriptExecutor) driver).executeScript("arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", element);
    element.click();
} catch (NoSuchElementException e) {
    Assert.fail("Button not found on page");
}

// Multi-catch (Java 7+)
try {
    readTestData("data.csv");
} catch (IOException | ParseException e) {
    logger.error("Data load failed", e);
}

finally

WebDriver driver = null;
try {
    driver = new ChromeDriver();
    runTests(driver);
} catch (WebDriverException e) {
    logger.error("Browser error", e);
} finally {
    // ALWAYS executes — even if return/exception in try or catch
    if (driver != null) {
        driver.quit();  // cleanup guaranteed
    }
}

throw — Manually Throw Exception

public void login(String user, String pass) {
    if (user == null || user.isEmpty()) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Username cannot be empty");
    }
    if (!isPageLoaded()) {
        throw new PageLoadException("Login page did not load within timeout");
    }
    // proceed with login
}

throws — Method Signature Declaration

public List<String[]> readCsvTestData(String filePath) throws IOException {
    List<String[]> data = new ArrayList<>();
    try (BufferedReader br = new BufferedReader(new FileReader(filePath))) {
        String line;
        while ((line = br.readLine()) != null) {
            data.add(line.split(","));
        }
    }
    return data;
}

// Caller must handle
@Test
public void dataDrivenTest() throws IOException {
    List<String[]> data = readCsvTestData("testdata.csv");
}

try-with-resources (Java 7+)

// AutoCloseable — resources closed automatically in reverse order
try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("config.properties");
     InputStreamReader isr = new InputStreamReader(fis);
     BufferedReader br = new BufferedReader(isr)) {
    Properties props = new Properties();
    props.load(br);
    return props;
}  // br, isr, fis all closed automatically — no finally needed

// Selenium — custom AutoCloseable wrapper
try (DriverSession session = new DriverSession("chrome")) {
    session.getDriver().get("https://example.com");
    runSmokeTests(session.getDriver());
}  // driver.quit() called in close()

Custom Exceptions

// Base framework exception
public class FrameworkException extends RuntimeException {
    public FrameworkException(String message) {
        super(message);
    }
    public FrameworkException(String message, Throwable cause) {
        super(message, cause);
    }
}

// Specific exceptions
public class InvalidConfigException extends FrameworkException {
    public InvalidConfigException(String message) {
        super("Config Error: " + message);
    }
}

public class PageLoadException extends FrameworkException {
    private final String pageName;
    private final int timeoutSeconds;

    public PageLoadException(String pageName, int timeoutSeconds) {
        super(String.format("Page '%s' did not load within %d seconds", pageName, timeoutSeconds));
        this.pageName = pageName;
        this.timeoutSeconds = timeoutSeconds;
    }

    public String getPageName() { return pageName; }
    public int getTimeoutSeconds() { return timeoutSeconds; }
}

// Usage in framework
public class HomePage extends BasePage {
    public void waitForLoad() {
        try {
            wait.until(ExpectedConditions.titleContains("Home"));
        } catch (TimeoutException e) {
            throw new PageLoadException("HomePage", 30);
        }
    }
}

public class ConfigReader {
    public static String getRequired(String key) {
        String value = properties.getProperty(key);
        if (value == null) {
            throw new InvalidConfigException("Missing required property: " + key);
        }
        return value;
    }
}

Selenium Exceptions

NoSuchElementException

Cause: Locator doesn't match any DOM element.
Example: driver.findElement(By.id("nonExistent"))
Fix: Verify locator, add explicit waits, check iframe context.

WebElement el = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10))
