A: Simply instantiate ChromeDriver — Selenium Manager handles driver download: WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();

Q2: What is the difference between get() and navigate().to()?

A: Both load a URL and wait for page load. navigate().to() is part of the Navigation interface which also provides back(), forward(), and refresh().

Q3: How do you run tests in headless mode?

A: Add options.addArguments("--headless=new") to ChromeOptions before creating ChromeDriver.

Q4: What is ChromeOptions used for?

A: ChromeOptions configures Chrome browser behavior — headless mode, notifications, incognito, custom profiles, extensions, window size, and more.

Q5: How do you maximize the browser window?

A: driver.manage().window().maximize() or add --start-maximized to ChromeOptions.

Q6: How do you delete all cookies?

A: driver.manage().deleteAllCookies() — useful for ensuring clean test state between tests.

Q7: What are the three types of timeouts in Selenium?

A: Implicit wait (findElement polling), page load timeout (page load completion), and script timeout (async JavaScript execution).

Q8: How do you set a custom browser window size?

A: driver.manage().window().setSize(new Dimension(1280, 720))

Q9: What is the difference between close() and quit()?

A: close() closes the current browser window. quit() closes all windows and terminates the WebDriver session, releasing all resources.

Q10: How do you configure Firefox with a custom profile?

A: Use ProfilesIni to load a profile, set preferences on FirefoxProfile, then pass it to FirefoxOptions via setProfile().

Q11: When should you use headless mode?

A: CI/CD pipelines, Docker containers, server environments without GUI, and when speed is prioritized over visual debugging.

Q12: How do you disable browser notifications in Chrome?

A: options.addArguments("--disable-notifications") in ChromeOptions.

Section 17: Locators

Most Important Topic: Locators are in the top 3 most-asked Selenium interview topics. Master all 8 locator strategies, CSS/XPath syntax, and dynamic element handling.

Locator Strategy — Priority Order

PriorityLocatorSpeedWhen to Use
1 (Best)IDFastestUnique, stable element IDs
2NameFastForm fields with name attribute
3CSS SelectorFastComplex selections, readable syntax
4XPathSlowerText-based search, traversing DOM
5LinkTextFastExact anchor text match
6PartialLinkTextFastPartial anchor text
7ClassNameFastSingle class, first match only
8 (Avoid)TagNameFastGeneric tags, multiple elements

1. ID Locator

WebElement email = driver.findElement(By.id("email"));
  • Pros: Fastest locator, unique by HTML spec, most reliable
  • Cons: Not all elements have IDs; dynamic IDs (React/Vue) change on reload
  • When to use: Elements with stable, unique id attributes

2. Name Locator

WebElement username = driver.findElement(By.name("username"));
  • Pros: Fast, commonly available on form fields
  • Cons: May not be unique; multiple elements can share the same name
  • When to use: Input fields, radio buttons, checkboxes in forms

3. ClassName Locator

WebElement btn = driver.findElement(By.className("btn-primary"));
  • Pros: Simple syntax for styled elements
  • Cons: Returns only the first match; compound classes need CSS/XPath; not unique
  • When to use: When class is unique and you need the first matching element

4. TagName Locator

List<WebElement> inputs = driver.findElements(By.tagName("input"));
  • Pros: Finds all elements of a type
  • Cons: Too generic; returns many elements; rarely unique
  • When to use: Counting elements, iterating all links/images

5. LinkText Locator

WebElement signIn = driver.findElement(By.linkText("Sign In"));
  • Pros: Exact match, human-readable, fast
  • Cons: Case-sensitive; must match entire visible text; only works on <a> tags
  • When to use: Navigation links with exact, stable text

6. PartialLinkText Locator

WebElement link = driver.findElement(By.partialLinkText("Sign"));
  • Pros: Flexible partial matching
  • Cons: May match multiple links; less precise
  • When to use: Long link text where only part is stable

7. CSS Selector — Comprehensive Guide

Basic Selectors

// By tag
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("div"));

// By ID
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("#email"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input#email"));

// By class
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector(".btn-primary"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input.btn-primary"));

Attribute Selectors

// Single attribute
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input[type='text']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[name='email']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[data-testid='submit-btn']"));

// Multiple attributes
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input[type='text'][name='email']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("button[type='submit'][class='btn']"));

Partial Attribute Matching

// Contains (*=)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[class*='partial']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[id*='user-input']"));

// Starts with (^=)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[class^='start']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[id^='user']"));

// Ends with ($=)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[class$='end']"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[src$='.png']"));

Combinators

// Direct child (>)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("div.form-group > input"));

// Descendant (space)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("div.container input"));

// Adjacent sibling (+)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("label + input"));

// General sibling (~)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("h1 ~ p"));

Pseudo-classes

// Nth child
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("tr:nth-child(2)"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("li:nth-child(odd)"));

// First/Last child
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("li:first-child"));
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("li:last-child"));

// Not selector
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input:not([type='hidden'])"));

8. XPath — Comprehensive Guide

Types of XPath

// ABSOLUTE XPath — AVOID! Brittle, breaks with any DOM change
driver.findElement(By.xpath("/html/body/div[1]/form/input[2]"));

// RELATIVE XPath — Preferred
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']"));

Attribute-based XPath

// Exact attribute match
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//button[@type='submit']"));

// Multiple attributes (AND)
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@type='text' and @name='email']"));

// Multiple attributes (OR)
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email' or @name='email']"));

// Contains
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[contains(@class,'partial')]"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[contains(@id,'user')]"));

// Starts-with
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[starts-with(@id,'user')]"));

// Ends-with (XPath 2.0 — limited browser support, use contains instead)
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[substring(@id, string-length(@id) - 2) = 'end']"));

Text-based XPath

// Exact text
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//button[text()='Submit']"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//a[text()='Sign In']"));

// Contains text
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//span[contains(text(),'Welcome')]"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[contains(text(),'Error')]"));

// Normalize space (handles extra whitespace)
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//button[normalize-space()='Submit']"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//label[normalize-space(text())='Email Address']"));

XPath Axes

// Parent
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']/parent::div"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']/.."));

// Child
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[@class='form']/child::input"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[@class='form']/input"));

// Ancestor
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']/ancestor::form"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//span/ancestor::div[@class='container']"));

// Descendant
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[@id='form']/descendant::input"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[@id='form']//input"));

// Following sibling
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//label[@for='email']/following-sibling::input"));

// Preceding sibling
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[@id='email']/preceding-sibling::label"));

Indexed XPath

// Select the 2nd input of type text
driver.findElement(By.xpath("(//input[@type='text'])[2]"));

// Last element
driver.findElement(By.xpath("(//div[@class='item'])[last()]"));

CSS vs XPath Comparison

AspectCSS SelectorXPath
PerformanceFaster (native browser engine)Slower (XPath engine traversal)
DirectionForward only (parent → child)Bidirectional (parent, child, sibling, ancestor)
Text SearchNot supportedtext(), contains(text()), normalize-space()
ReadabilityMore readable, shorterMore verbose, powerful
Browser SupportAll browsersAll browsers (slight differences)
Shadow DOMLimited (needs pierce selector)Cannot pierce shadow DOM either
Complex TraversalLimited to child/descendant/siblingFull axis support (ancestor, following, preceding)
Dynamic IDs[id*='partial'] works wellcontains(@id,'partial') works well
Index Selection:nth-child(n)(//element)[n]

Dynamic Element Strategies

// Strategy 1: Partial attribute match (dynamic IDs)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[id*='user-email']"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//input[contains(@id,'user-email')]"));

// Strategy 2: Parent-child relationship
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("div.login-form > input[type='email']"));
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//div[@class='login-form']//input[@type='email']"));

// Strategy 3: Sibling relationship
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//label[text()='Email']/following-sibling::input"));

// Strategy 4: Index-based (last resort)
driver.findElement(By.xpath("(//input[@type='text'])[1]"));

// Strategy 5: data-testid attribute (best practice for test automation)
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[data-testid='login-email']"));

Locator Best Practices

  1. Prefer ID when available and stable — fastest and most reliable.
  2. Use CSS over XPath for performance when text search is not needed.
  3. Avoid absolute XPath — breaks with any DOM structure change.
  4. Use data-testid attributes — designed for automation, stable across UI changes.
  5. Never use dynamic IDs directly — use partial match or parent-child strategy.
  6. Keep locators short and readable — if a locator is 200 characters, refactor the HTML or use a better strategy.
  7. Avoid indexing when possible — (//input)[3] breaks when order changes.
  8. Store locators in Page Object classes — single point of maintenance.
  9. Test locators in browser DevTools — use document.querySelector() or $x() in console.
  10. Use unique, descriptive locator names in Page Objects — EMAIL_INPUT, not INPUT1.

Selenium 4 Relative Locators

import static org.openqa.selenium.support.locators.RelativeLocator.*;

WebElement password = driver.findElement(By.id("password"));

// Find element below the password field
WebElement confirmPwd = driver.findElement(with(By.id("confirm-password"))
    .below(password));

// Find element above
WebElement username = driver.findElement(with(By.id("username"))
    .above(password));

// Find element to the right
WebElement submitBtn = driver.findElement(with(By.id("submit"))
    .toRightOf(password));

// Find element to the left
WebElement cancelBtn = driver.findElement(with(By.id("cancel"))
    .toLeftOf(submitBtn));

// Find element near (within 50 pixels)
WebElement errorMsg = driver.findElement(with(By.className("error"))
    .near(password, 50));

findElement vs findElements

AspectfindElement()findElements()
Return typeWebElement (single)List<WebElement> (collection)
No match foundThrows NoSuchElementExceptionReturns empty list (size 0)
Multiple matchesReturns first match onlyReturns all matches
Use caseUnique elements (buttons, inputs)Lists, tables, multiple items

Real DOM Examples

Example HTML

<div class="login-container" data-testid="login-form">
  <label for="email">Email Address</label>
  <input type="email" id="user-email-input" name="email" placeholder="Enter email">
  <label for="password">Password</label>
  <input type="password" id="user-password" name="password">
  <button type="submit" class="btn btn-primary">Sign In</button>
  <a href="/forgot">Forgot Password?</a>
</div>

Locator Solutions

// Email input — multiple valid approaches
driver.findElement(By.id("user-email-input"));                          // Best
driver.findElement(By.name("email"));                                   // Good
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("input[type='email']"));                // Good
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("[data-testid='login-form'] input[type='email']")); // Scoped
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//label[text()='Email Address']/following-sibling::input"));

// Sign In button
driver.findElement(By.xpath("//button[text()='Sign In']"));               // Text-based
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("button.btn-primary"));                 // CSS class
driver.findElement(By.cssSelector("button[type='submit']"));              // Attribute

// Forgot Password link
driver.findElement(By.linkText("Forgot Password?"));                      // Exact link text
driver.findElement(By.partialLinkText("Forgot"));                         // Partial

Interview Q&A — Locators

Q1: What are the 8 locator strategies in Selenium?

A: ID, Name, ClassName, TagName, LinkText, PartialLinkText, CSS Selector, and XPath.

Q2: Which locator is fastest?

A: ID is the fastest because browsers index elements by ID internally. CSS Selector is the second fastest.

Q3: What is the difference between CSS Selector and XPath?

A: CSS is faster and forward-only. XPath is slower but supports bidirectional traversal and text-based searches.

Q4: When would you use XPath over CSS?

A: When you need to find elements by visible text, traverse up to parent/ancestor elements, or navigate between siblings.

Q5: What is the difference between findElement and findElements?

A: findElement returns a single WebElement (throws exception if not found). findElements returns a List (empty list if none found).

Q6: How do you handle dynamic IDs?

A: Use partial attribute matching: CSS [id*='partial'] or XPath contains(@id,'partial'). Alternatively, use parent-child or sibling relationships.

Q7: Why should you avoid absolute XPath?

A: Absolute XPath (/html/body/div[1]/...) breaks whenever any element is added or removed from the DOM hierarchy above the target element.

Q8: What are relative locators in Selenium 4?

A: above(), below(), toLeftOf(), toRightOf(), and near() — locate elements based on spatial relationship to a reference element.

Q9: How do you locate an element by its text?

A: XPath only: //button[text()='Submit'] or //span[contains(text(),'Welcome')]. CSS cannot search by text.

Q10: What is normalize-space() in XPath?

A: Strips leading/trailing whitespace and collapses internal whitespace. Useful when element text has inconsistent spacing: //button[normalize-space()='Submit']

Q11: How do you select the nth element when multiple match?

A: CSS: li:nth-child(3). XPath: (//li)[3]. Index is 1-based in both.

Q12: What is a data-testid attribute and why use it?

A: A custom HTML attribute added specifically for test automation. Stable across UI refactors since it is not tied to styling or behavior.

Q13: Can ClassName locator find multiple classes?

A: No. By.className("btn-primary") only accepts a single class. For compound classes, use CSS: .btn.btn-primary.

Q14: How do you locate elements inside a shadow DOM?

A: Standard locators cannot pierce shadow DOM. Use Selenium 4's getShadowRoot() or JavaScript execution to access shadow DOM elements.

Q15: What is the difference between child (>) and descendant (space) in CSS?

A: Child (>) selects direct children only. Descendant (space) selects all nested descendants at any depth.

Q16: How do you write an XPath for a button with text "Submit" inside a form?

A: //form//button[text()='Submit'] or //form/button[normalize-space()='Submit']

Q17: What locator strategy do you use for a table row by cell content?

A: XPath: //td[text()='John']/parent::tr or //tr[td[text()='John']]

Q18: How do you verify a locator finds exactly one element?

A: Use findElements and assert size: assert driver.findElements(by).size() == 1; Or test in browser DevTools console.

Q19: What is the following-sibling axis in XPath?

A: Selects all sibling elements that appear after the current element: //label[@for='email']/following-sibling::input

Q20: CSS selector for input with type text AND name email?

A: input[type='text'][name='email']

Q21: How do you locate a disabled button?

A: CSS: button[disabled] or button:disabled. XPath: //button[@disabled]

Q22: What is the best locator strategy priority order?

A: ID → Name → CSS Selector → XPath → LinkText → PartialLinkText → ClassName → TagName

Section 18: WebElement Commands

WebElement Interface

A WebElement represents a DOM element on the web page. It extends SearchContext, meaning you can call findElement/findElements on a WebElement to scope searches within that element.

Action Commands

click()

WebElement loginBtn = driver.findElement(By.id("login"));
loginBtn.click();  // Click the element

When to use: Buttons, links, checkboxes, radio buttons, any clickable element.

sendKeys()

WebElement email = driver.findElement(By.id("email"));
email.sendKeys("user@example.com");

// Clear before typing
email.clear();
email.sendKeys("new@example.com");

// Upload file (send absolute file path)
WebElement fileInput = driver.findElement(By.id("file-upload"));
fileInput.sendKeys("C:/Users/test/document.pdf");

// Keyboard actions combined
email.sendKeys(Keys.TAB);
email.sendKeys(Keys.CONTROL + "a");  // Select all
email.sendKeys(Keys.DELETE);

When to use: Text inputs, textareas, file uploads, keyboard shortcuts.

clear()

WebElement searchBox = driver.findElement(By.id("search"));
searchBox.clear();  // Clears the text field

When to use: Before entering new text in pre-filled fields.

submit()

WebElement form = driver.findElement(By.id("login-form"));
form.submit();  // Submits the form (deprecated behavior in modern apps)

Note: submit() triggers form submission. In modern SPAs, prefer clicking the submit button instead.

Query Commands

WebElement element = driver.findElement(By.id("email"));

// Visible text content
String text = element.getText();

// HTML attribute value
String id = element.getAttribute("id");
String value = element.getAttribute("value");
String href = element.getAttribute("href");

// CSS property value
String color = element.getCssValue("color");
String fontSize = element.getCssValue("font-size");
String bgColor = element.getCssValue("background-color");

// HTML tag name
String tag = element.getTagName();  // "input", "button", "div"

// Element dimensions
Dimension size = element.getSize();  // width, height

// Element coordinates
Point location = element.getLocation();  // x, y

// Combined size + location (Selenium 4)
Rectangle rect = element.getRect();  // x, y, width, height

State Commands

WebElement checkbox = driver.findElement(By.id("agree"));
WebElement submitBtn = driver.findElement(By.id("submit"));
WebElement hiddenDiv = driver.findElement(By.id("popup"));

boolean isVisible = hiddenDiv.isDisplayed();   // false if hidden via CSS
boolean isActive = submitBtn.isEnabled();     // false if disabled attribute set
boolean isChecked = checkbox.isSelected();    // true if checkbox/radio is checked
MethodReturns true whenCommon use
isDisplayed()Element is visible on pageVerify element visibility after action
isEnabled()Element is not disabledCheck if button is clickable
isSelected()Checkbox/radio is checkedVerify selection state

Chaining Locators on WebElement

// Scope search within a parent element
WebElement form = driver.findElement(By.id("login-form"));
WebElement email = form.findElement(By.name("email"));
WebElement password = form.findElement(By.name("password"));
WebElement submit = form.findElement(By.cssSelector("button[type='submit']"));

Multiple Elements

// Find all matching elements
List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector("table tr"));

// Iterate with for-each
for (WebElement row : rows) {
    System.out.println(row.getText());
}

// Iterate with streams
rows.stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .filter(text -> text.contains("Active"))
    .forEach(System.out::println);

// Get count
int rowCount = rows.size();

// Access by index
WebElement firstRow = rows.get(0);
WebElement lastRow = rows.get(rows.size() - 1);

Selenium 4 Additions

WebElement element = driver.findElement(By.id("submit-btn"));

// Accessibility role (e.g., "button", "textbox", "link")
String role = element.getAriaRole();

// Accessible name (aria-label or associated label text)
String name = element.getAccessibleName();

// DOM attribute (exact HTML attribute)
String domAttr = element.getDomAttribute("class");

// DOM property (live JavaScript property value)
String domProp = element.getDomProperty("value");

Common Mistake: Using getText() on an <input> field returns empty string. Use getAttribute("value") or getDomProperty("value") to get the input's current value.

WebElement input = driver.findElement(By.id("email"));
input.sendKeys("test@example.com");

String text = input.getText();              // Returns "" (empty!)
String value = input.getAttribute("value"); // Returns "test@example.com"
String prop = input.getDomProperty("value"); // Returns "test@example.com"

Interview Q&A — WebElement Commands

Q1: What is a WebElement in Selenium?

A: A WebElement represents a single DOM element on the web page. It provides methods to interact with (click, sendKeys) and query (getText, getAttribute) the element.

Q2: What is the difference between getText() and getAttribute("value")?

A: getText() returns the visible text content between tags (for labels, divs, spans). getAttribute("value") returns the value attribute of input fields.

Q3: How do you upload a file in Selenium?

A: Find the file input element and use sendKeys with the absolute file path: fileInput.sendKeys("C:/path/to/file.pdf")

Q4: What is the difference between isDisplayed() and isEnabled()?

A: isDisplayed() checks if the element is visible on the page. isEnabled() checks if the element is interactive (not disabled).

Q5: Can you call findElement on a WebElement?

A: Yes. WebElement extends SearchContext, so you can chain locators to scope searches within a parent element.

Q6: What does isSelected() check?

A: Whether a checkbox, radio button, or option element is currently selected/checked.

Q7: What is getRect() in Selenium 4?

A: Returns a Rectangle object containing both the element's position (x, y) and dimensions (width, height) in a single call.

Q8: What is the difference between getAttribute() and getDomProperty()?

A: getAttribute() returns the HTML attribute as written in the source. getDomProperty() returns the live JavaScript property value, which may differ (e.g., after user input).

Q9: How do you get all links on a page?

A: List<WebElement> links = driver.findElements(By.tagName("a"));

Q10: What happens if you call click() on a hidden element?

A: Selenium throws ElementNotInteractableException because the element is not visible/clickable on the page.

Q11: How do you get the CSS color of an element?

A: element.getCssValue("color") returns the computed CSS property value as a string (e.g., "rgba(255, 0, 0, 1)").

Q12: What is getAccessibleName() used for?

A: Returns the accessible name of an element for accessibility testing — either the aria-label or the associated label text.

Section 19: Waits

Critical Topic: Waits are in the top 3 most-asked Selenium interview topics. Understanding implicit, explicit, and fluent waits — and when to use each — is essential.

Why Waits?

Modern web applications are dynamic — content loads via AJAX, animations play, elements appear/disappear. Without waits, tests fail with NoSuchElementException or ElementNotInteractableException because Selenium tries to interact before the element is ready.

Thread.sleep() — Anti-Pattern

// NEVER DO THIS in production tests
Thread.sleep(5000);  // Hard-coded 5 second pause
  • Wastes time: Always waits the full duration even if element is ready sooner.
  • Flaky: May not wait long enough on slow networks.
  • Not scalable: Cannot adjust dynamically to page load conditions.

Implicit Wait

driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(Duration.ofSeconds(10));

How it works: When findElement() is called, if the element is not immediately found, Selenium polls the DOM repeatedly (default every 500ms) until the element appears or the timeout expires.

  • Set once per driver session — applies to all subsequent findElement/findElements calls.
  • Pros: Simple, global, no extra code per element.
  • Cons: Applies same timeout to all elements; cannot wait for specific conditions (clickable, visible); slows down tests when elements don't exist.

Explicit Wait

import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.WebDriverWait;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.ExpectedConditions;
import java.time.Duration;

WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
WebElement element = wait.until(
    ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("dashboard"))
);

Common ExpectedConditions

WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));

// Element visible in DOM and displayed
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("result")));

// Element present in DOM (may not be visible)
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.presenceOfElementLocated(By.id("hidden-div")));

// Element visible AND enabled (ready to click)
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(By.id("submit")));

// Element disappears
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.invisibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("spinner")));

// Specific text appears in element
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.textToBePresentInElementLocated(
    By.id("status"), "Success"));

// Page title checks
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.titleContains("Dashboard"));
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.titleIs("My App - Dashboard"));

// Alert appears
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());

// Frame available and switch to it
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt("iframe-id"));

// Number of browser windows
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.numberOfWindowsToBe(2));

// Element becomes stale (removed from DOM)
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.stalenessOf(oldElement));

// URL checks
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.urlContains("/dashboard"));
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.urlToBe("https://app.example.com/dashboard"));

Custom ExpectedCondition

// Wait until list has at least 5 items
wait.until(driver -> driver.findElements(By.cssSelector("li.item")).size() >= 5);

// Wait until element text changes
wait.until(driver -> {
    WebElement el = driver.findElement(By.id("counter"));
    return Integer.parseInt(el.getText()) > 0;
});

Fluent Wait

import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.FluentWait;
import org.openqa.selenium.NoSuchElementException;

FluentWait<WebDriver> fluentWait = new FluentWait<>(driver)
    .withTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(30))
    .pollingEvery(Duration.ofMillis(500))
    .ignoring(NoSuchElementException.class)
    .ignoring(StaleElementReferenceException.class);

WebElement element = fluentWait.until(driver ->
    driver.findElement(By.id("dynamic-content"))
);

When to use: Irregular load times, animations, elements that may throw transient exceptions during loading.

Wait Comparison

AspectImplicit WaitExplicit WaitFluent Wait
ScopeGlobal (all findElement calls)Specific element/conditionSpecific element/condition
ConfigurationSingle timeout valueTimeout + ExpectedConditionTimeout + polling + ignored exceptions
Polling interval500ms (fixed)500ms (fixed)Customizable
Condition typesElement presence onlyAny condition (visible, clickable, text, etc.)Custom lambda conditions
Exception handlingThrows on timeoutThrows on timeoutCan ignore specific exceptions
PerformanceSlows all lookupsEfficient — waits only when neededEfficient with custom polling
Recommended?Set low (0-5s) or zeroYes — primary strategyFor special cases
Mix with others?Never mix with explicitBest used aloneNever mix with implicit

NEVER mix implicit and explicit waits! They add together unpredictably. If implicit wait is 10s and explicit wait is 10s, a single explicit wait call could take up to 20s. Set implicit wait to 0 when using explicit waits.

WaitUtils Utility Class

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;

public class WaitUtils {
    private WebDriver driver;
    private WebDriverWait wait;

    public WaitUtils(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(15));
    }

    public WebElement waitForVisible(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
    }

    public WebElement waitForClickable(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator));
    }

    public WebElement waitForPresence(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.presenceOfElementLocated(locator));
    }

    public boolean waitForInvisible(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.invisibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
    }

    public boolean waitForText(By locator, String text) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.textToBePresentInElementLocated(locator, text));
    }

    public Alert waitForAlert() {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());
    }

    public void waitForUrlContains(String partialUrl) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.urlContains(partialUrl));
    }

    public void waitForTitleContains(String title) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.titleContains(title));
    }

    public void waitForFrameAndSwitch(String frameId) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt(frameId));
    }

    public void waitForWindowCount(int count) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.numberOfWindowsToBe(count));
    }
}

Page Load and Script Timeouts

// Page load timeout — max time to wait for page to fully load
driver.manage().timeouts().pageLoadTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(30));

// Script timeout — max time for async JavaScript to execute
driver.manage().timeouts().scriptTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(20));

Interview Q&A — Waits

Q1: What are the types of waits in Selenium?

A: Implicit wait, explicit wait (WebDriverWait), and fluent wait (FluentWait). Thread.sleep() is not a Selenium wait — it is a Java pause and should be avoided.

Q2: What is the difference between implicit and explicit wait?

A: Implicit wait is set globally and polls for element presence on every findElement call. Explicit wait waits for a specific condition on a specific element with a defined timeout.

Q3: Why should you never use Thread.sleep()?

A: It wastes time (always waits full duration), makes tests flaky (may not wait long enough), and cannot adapt to varying load times.

Q4: Why should you never mix implicit and explicit waits?

A: Their timeouts add together unpredictably. An explicit wait of 10s with implicit wait of 10s could take up to 20s total, causing tests to hang.

Q5: What is the difference between visibilityOfElementLocated and presenceOfElementLocated?

A: presenceOfElementLocated checks if element exists in DOM (may be hidden). visibilityOfElementLocated checks if element exists AND is visible (not hidden via CSS).

Q6: What is elementToBeClickable?

A: Waits until the element is both visible and enabled — ready to receive a click event. Most reliable condition before clicking.

Q7: What is stalenessOf in ExpectedConditions?

A: Waits until a previously located element is removed from the DOM. Useful after actions that refresh part of the page (e.g., AJAX table refresh).

Q8: What is FluentWait?

A: A configurable wait with custom polling interval and ability to ignore specific exceptions during polling. More flexible than WebDriverWait.

Q9: What is the default polling frequency for WebDriverWait?

A: 500 milliseconds — Selenium checks the condition every 500ms until timeout or condition is met.

Q10: How do you wait for a page to load completely?

A: Set pageLoadTimeout: driver.manage().timeouts().pageLoadTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(30)). Or use explicit wait on a known element that appears after load.

Q11: What is a custom ExpectedCondition?

A: A lambda expression passed to wait.until() that returns true when the custom condition is met: wait.until(driver -> driver.findElements(by).size() > 5)

Q12: What happens when an explicit wait times out?

A: Selenium throws TimeoutException. The test should catch this or let the framework report the failure.

Q13: Should implicit wait be set to zero?

A: Best practice when using explicit waits: set implicit wait to 0 or a very low value (1-2s) to avoid timeout stacking.

Q14: How do you wait for an element's text to change?

A: Use textToBePresentInElementLocated or a custom condition: wait.until(ExpectedConditions.textToBePresentInElementLocated(by, "Expected Text"))

Q15: What is the recommended wait strategy for a test framework?

A: Set implicit wait to 0. Use explicit waits via a WaitUtils utility class for all element interactions. Use fluent wait only for special cases with irregular timing.

Q16: How do you wait for an AJAX call to complete?

A: Wait for a loading spinner to disappear: wait.until(ExpectedConditions.invisibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("spinner"))) or wait for the result element to appear.

Q17: What is scriptTimeout used for?

A: Sets the maximum time Selenium waits for asynchronous JavaScript (executeAsyncScript) to complete before throwing TimeoutException.

Section 20: Dropdowns

HTML Select Dropdowns — The Select Class

For standard HTML <select> elements, Selenium provides the Select class with built-in methods.

import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.Select;

WebElement dropdownElement = driver.findElement(By.id("country"));
Select dropdown = new Select(dropdownElement);

Selection Methods

// Select by visible text (exact match)
dropdown.selectByVisibleText("United States");

// Select by value attribute
dropdown.selectByValue("US");

// Select by index (0-based)
dropdown.selectByIndex(0);  // First option

Deselection Methods (Multi-select only)

// Deselect all selected options
dropdown.deselectAll();

// Deselect by visible text
dropdown.deselectByVisibleText("United States");

// Deselect by value
dropdown.deselectByValue("US");

// Deselect by index
dropdown.deselectByIndex(0);

Getter Methods

// All options in the dropdown
List<WebElement> allOptions = dropdown.getOptions();

// All currently selected options
List<WebElement> selected = dropdown.getAllSelectedOptions();

// First selected option (single-select)
WebElement firstSelected = dropdown.getFirstSelectedOption();
String selectedText = firstSelected.getText();

// Check if multi-select
boolean isMulti = dropdown.isMultiple();

Multi-Select Dropdowns

WebElement multiSelect = driver.findElement(By.id("skills"));
Select skills = new Select(multiSelect);

if (skills.isMultiple()) {
    skills.selectByVisibleText("Java");
    skills.selectByVisibleText("Python");
    skills.selectByVisibleText("Selenium");

    List<WebElement> selected = skills.getAllSelectedOptions();
    System.out.println("Selected: " + selected.size() + " skills");
}

Non-Select Dropdowns (Bootstrap / React / Custom)

Modern frameworks use <div> or <ul> elements instead of <select>. The Select class does not work — handle with click actions.

// Step 1: Click to open the dropdown
WebElement dropdownTrigger = driver.findElement(By.id("custom-dropdown"));
dropdownTrigger.click();

// Step 2: Wait for options to appear
WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(5));
WebElement option = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(
    By.xpath("//ul[@class='dropdown-menu']//li[text()='Option 2']")
));

// Step 3: Click the desired option
option.click();

Auto-Suggest / Typeahead Dropdowns

WebElement searchInput = driver.findElement(By.id("city-search"));

// Type to trigger suggestions
searchInput.sendKeys("New Y");

// Wait for suggestions to appear
WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(5));
WebElement suggestion = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(
    By.xpath("//ul[@class='suggestions']//li[contains(text(),'New York')]")
));

// Select the suggestion
suggestion.click();

Complete Example — All Dropdown Types

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;
import java.util.List;

public class DropdownHandler {
    WebDriver driver;
    WebDriverWait wait;

    public DropdownHandler(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    // Standard HTML select dropdown
    public void selectByText(By locator, String text) {
        Select select = new Select(driver.findElement(locator));
        select.selectByVisibleText(text);
    }

    public void selectByValue(By locator, String value) {
        Select select = new Select(driver.findElement(locator));
        select.selectByValue(value);
    }

    // Custom/Bootstrap dropdown
    public void selectCustomOption(By dropdownLocator, String optionText) {
        driver.findElement(dropdownLocator).click();
        By optionLocator = By.xpath(
            "//ul[contains(@class,'dropdown')]//li[normalize-space()='" + optionText + "']"
        );
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(optionLocator)).click();
    }

    // Auto-suggest dropdown
    public void selectAutoSuggest(By inputLocator, String partialText, String fullText) {
        WebElement input = driver.findElement(inputLocator);
        input.clear();
        input.sendKeys(partialText);
        By suggestion = By.xpath(
            "//ul[contains(@class,'suggest')]//li[contains(text(),'" + fullText + "')]"
        );
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(suggestion)).click();
    }

    // Get all options from standard select
    public List<String> getAllOptions(By locator) {
        Select select = new Select(driver.findElement(locator));
        return select.getOptions().stream()
            .map(WebElement::getText)
            .toList();
    }
}

Interview Q&A — Dropdowns

Q1: How do you handle dropdowns in Selenium?

A: For HTML <select> elements, use the Select class. For custom/Bootstrap dropdowns, click to open and then click the desired option.

Q2: What are the three ways to select an option in a dropdown?

A: selectByVisibleText(), selectByValue(), and selectByIndex().

Q3: Can you use Select class on a div-based dropdown?

A: No. Select class only works with HTML <select> elements. Div/ul-based dropdowns require click-based interaction.

Q4: How do you handle multi-select dropdowns?

A: Check isMultiple(), then call selectByVisibleText() multiple times for each option. Use getAllSelectedOptions() to verify.

Q5: How do you get all options from a dropdown?

A: dropdown.getOptions() returns a List<WebElement> of all options.

Q6: What happens if you call deselectAll() on a single-select dropdown?

A: Selenium throws UnsupportedOperationException because single-select dropdowns cannot be deselected.

Q7: How do you handle auto-suggest dropdowns?

A: Type partial text with sendKeys(), wait for suggestions to appear, then click the matching suggestion element.

Q8: How do you verify the selected option in a dropdown?

A: dropdown.getFirstSelectedOption().getText() for single-select, or getAllSelectedOptions() for multi-select.

Q9: What is the difference between selectByVisibleText and selectByValue?

A: selectByVisibleText matches the displayed text between <option> tags. selectByValue matches the value attribute of the <option> element.

Q10: How do you select an option that is not visible (needs scrolling)?

A: Use selectByValue() or selectByIndex() which don't require the option to be visible. Or scroll the dropdown first using JavaScript.

Section 21: Alerts

Alert Types

Alert TypeDescriptionMethods Available
Simple AlertMessage + OK buttonaccept(), getText()
Confirmation AlertMessage + OK + Cancelaccept(), dismiss(), getText()
Prompt AlertMessage + text input + OK + Cancelaccept(), dismiss(), getText(), sendKeys()

Switching to Alert

// Switch to alert — MUST do this before interacting
Alert alert = driver.switchTo().alert();

Alert Methods

Alert alert = driver.switchTo().alert();

// Get alert message text
String message = alert.getText();
System.out.println("Alert says: " + message);

// Click OK button
alert.accept();

// Click Cancel button (confirmation/prompt only)
alert.dismiss();

// Type text in prompt alert
alert.sendKeys("My input text");
alert.accept();

Complete Alert Handling Examples

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;

public class AlertHandler {
    WebDriver driver;
    WebDriverWait wait;

    public AlertHandler(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    // Handle simple alert — click OK
    public String handleSimpleAlert() {
        Alert alert = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());
        String text = alert.getText();
        alert.accept();
        return text;
    }

    // Handle confirmation alert — click OK or Cancel
    public void handleConfirmationAlert(boolean accept) {
        Alert alert = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());
        if (accept) {
            alert.accept();
        } else {
            alert.dismiss();
        }
    }

    // Handle prompt alert — enter text and submit
    public void handlePromptAlert(String inputText) {
        Alert alert = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());
        alert.sendKeys(inputText);
        alert.accept();
    }
}

Wait for Alert

WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
Alert alert = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent());
alert.accept();

JavaScript Alerts vs Authentication Popups

AspectJavaScript AlertAuthentication Popup
Triggered byJavaScript alert(), confirm(), prompt()HTTP Basic/Digest Auth
Handled bydriver.switchTo().alert()URL embedding: https://user:pass@host
AppearanceBrowser-native dialogBrowser login dialog
Selenium supportFull Alert APINot via Alert API — use URL or CDP

Handling Unexpected Alerts

try {
    driver.findElement(By.id("submit")).click();
    // Perform actions...
} catch (UnhandledAlertException e) {
    // Unexpected alert appeared — dismiss it
    driver.switchTo().alert().dismiss();
    // Retry or log the issue
}

Sweet Alert / Bootstrap Modals — Not Real Alerts

Important: SweetAlert, Bootstrap modals, and custom popup dialogs are NOT JavaScript alerts. They are regular HTML elements in the DOM. Handle them with normal locators — do NOT use switchTo().alert().

// SweetAlert / Bootstrap modal — use regular locators
WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(5));

// Wait for modal to appear
WebElement modal = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(
    By.cssSelector(".swal2-popup, .modal-dialog")
));

// Read modal text
String modalText = modal.findElement(By.cssSelector(".swal2-content, .modal-body")).getText();

// Click OK/Confirm button
modal.findElement(By.cssSelector(".swal2-confirm, .btn-primary")).click();

Interview Q&A — Alerts

Q1: How do you handle alerts in Selenium?

A: Switch to the alert using driver.switchTo().alert(), then use accept(), dismiss(), getText(), or sendKeys() as needed.

Q2: What are the three types of JavaScript alerts?

A: Simple alert (OK only), confirmation alert (OK + Cancel), and prompt alert (text input + OK + Cancel).

Q3: What is the difference between accept() and dismiss()?

A: accept() clicks OK. dismiss() clicks Cancel. dismiss() only works on confirmation and prompt alerts.

Q4: How do you enter text in a prompt alert?

A: alert.sendKeys("text") followed by alert.accept().

Q5: What is UnhandledAlertException?

A: Thrown when an unexpected alert appears while Selenium is trying to interact with the page. Handle by switching to alert and dismissing it.

Q6: Can you use switchTo().alert() for Bootstrap modals?

A: No. Bootstrap modals and SweetAlert are HTML elements, not JavaScript alerts. Use regular findElement locators to interact with them.

Q7: How do you wait for an alert to appear?

A: wait.until(ExpectedConditions.alertIsPresent())

Q8: How do you handle HTTP authentication popups?

A: Embed credentials in the URL: https://username:password@example.com. Or use Selenium 4 CDP to handle authentication.

Q9: What happens if you try to find an element while an alert is open?

A: Selenium throws UnhandledAlertException because the alert blocks interaction with the page DOM.

Q10: How do you verify alert text in a test?

A: String alertText = driver.switchTo().alert().getText(); then assert against expected text before accepting/dismissing.

Section 22: Frames & Windows

Frames (iFrames)

A frame (iframe) is an embedded HTML document within another HTML page. Selenium can only interact with elements in the currently focused frame — you must switch to a frame before locating elements inside it.

Switching to Frames

// By index (0-based)
driver.switchTo().frame(0);   // First frame on page
driver.switchTo().frame(1);   // Second frame

// By name or ID attribute
driver.switchTo().frame("frameName");
driver.switchTo().frame("iframe-id");

// By WebElement reference
WebElement frameElement = driver.findElement(By.id("my-frame"));
driver.switchTo().frame(frameElement);

Switching Back

// Return to main page content (top-level)
driver.switchTo().defaultContent();

// Return to parent frame (one level up)
driver.switchTo().parentFrame();
Main Page (defaultContent)
├── iframe#header (frame 0)
├── iframe#content (frame 1)
│   └── iframe#inner-form (nested frame)
│       └── <input id="email">  ← Must switch: defaultContent → frame 1 → inner-form
└── iframe#footer (frame 2)

Nested Frame Handling

// Switch to outer frame first, then inner frame
driver.switchTo().frame("content-frame");
driver.switchTo().frame("inner-form");

// Now interact with elements inside nested frame
driver.findElement(By.id("email")).sendKeys("test@example.com");

// Switch back to outer frame
driver.switchTo().parentFrame();

// Switch back to main page
driver.switchTo().defaultContent();

Wait for Frame

WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));

// Wait for frame and switch in one step
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt("frame-id"));
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt(0));
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt(
    By.id("my-frame")
));

Complete Frame Handling Code

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;

public class FrameHandler {
    WebDriver driver;
    WebDriverWait wait;

    public FrameHandler(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    public void interactWithNestedFrame() {
        // Switch to outer frame
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt("outer-frame"));

        // Switch to inner frame
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt("inner-frame"));

        // Interact with element inside nested frame
        WebElement email = wait.until(
            ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("email"))
        );
        email.sendKeys("user@example.com");

        WebElement submit = driver.findElement(By.id("submit"));
        submit.click();

        // Navigate back up
        driver.switchTo().parentFrame();  // Back to outer frame
        driver.switchTo().defaultContent(); // Back to main page
    }

    public void switchToFrameByElement(By locator) {
        WebElement frame = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.presenceOfElementLocated(locator));
        driver.switchTo().frame(frame);
    }
}

Windows and Tabs

Window Handles

// Current window handle
String currentHandle = driver.getWindowHandle();

// All open window handles
Set<String> allHandles = driver.getWindowHandles();
System.out.println("Open windows: " + allHandles.size());

Switching Windows

// Store parent window handle
String parentHandle = driver.getWindowHandle();

// Click link that opens new window/tab
driver.findElement(By.linkText("Open New Window")).click();

// Wait for new window
WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
wait.until(ExpectedConditions.numberOfWindowsToBe(2));

// Switch to new window
for (String handle : driver.getWindowHandles()) {
    if (!handle.equals(parentHandle)) {
        driver.switchTo().window(handle);
        break;
    }
}

// Perform actions in new window
System.out.println("New window title: " + driver.getTitle());
driver.findElement(By.id("action-btn")).click();

// Close new window and switch back to parent
driver.close();
driver.switchTo().window(parentHandle);

New Window/Tab (Selenium 4)

// Open a new tab
driver.switchTo().newWindow(WindowType.TAB);
driver.get("https://example.com");

// Open a new window
driver.switchTo().newWindow(WindowType.WINDOW);
driver.get("https://google.com");

close() vs quit()

MethodScopeSessionUse Case
close()Current window/tab onlySession remains activeClose popup after handling
quit()All windows/tabsSession terminatedEnd of test — always in @AfterMethod

Complete Multi-Window Handling

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;
import java.util.Set;

public class WindowHandler {
    WebDriver driver;
    WebDriverWait wait;

    public WindowHandler(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    public void handlePopupWindow(By triggerLocator) {
        String parentHandle = driver.getWindowHandle();

        // Click element that opens new window
        driver.findElement(triggerLocator).click();

        // Wait for new window to open
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.numberOfWindowsToBe(2));

        // Switch to new window
        switchToNewWindow(parentHandle);

        // Perform actions in popup
        System.out.println("Popup title: " + driver.getTitle());
        driver.findElement(By.id("confirm-btn")).click();

        // Close popup and return to parent
        driver.close();
        driver.switchTo().window(parentHandle);
    }

    private void switchToNewWindow(String parentHandle) {
        Set<String> handles = driver.getWindowHandles();
        for (String handle : handles) {
            if (!handle.equals(parentHandle)) {
                driver.switchTo().window(handle);
                return;
            }
        }
        throw new NoSuchWindowException("New window not found");
    }

    public void closeAllExcept(String keepHandle) {
        for (String handle : driver.getWindowHandles()) {
            if (!handle.equals(keepHandle)) {
                driver.switchTo().window(handle);
                driver.close();
            }
        }
        driver.switchTo().window(keepHandle);
    }
}

Handling Popups (Child Windows)

// Common pattern: store parent, switch to popup, act, close, return
String mainWindow = driver.getWindowHandle();
driver.findElement(By.id("print-preview")).click();

wait.until(ExpectedConditions.numberOfWindowsToBe(2));

for (String handle : driver.getWindowHandles()) {
    if (!handle.equals(mainWindow)) {
        driver.switchTo().window(handle);
        // Verify popup content
        assert driver.getTitle().contains("Print Preview");
        driver.close();
    }
}
driver.switchTo().window(mainWindow);

Interview Q&A — Frames & Windows

Q1: What is an iframe and why must you switch to it?

A: An iframe embeds a separate HTML document inside a page. Selenium's findElement only searches the current context — you must switchTo().frame() to access elements inside.

Q2: What are the three ways to switch to a frame?

A: By index (int), by name/id (String), or by WebElement reference.

Q3: What is the difference between defaultContent() and parentFrame()?

A: defaultContent() returns to the top-level page. parentFrame() returns one level up to the immediate parent frame.

Q4: How do you handle nested frames?

A: Switch to outer frame first, then inner frame. To exit, use parentFrame() to go up one level, or defaultContent() to return to the main page.

Q5: What is a window handle?

A: A unique string identifier assigned by the browser to each window/tab. Used with switchTo().window(handle) to switch between windows.

Q6: What is the difference between close() and quit()?

A: close() closes the current window only. quit() closes all windows and terminates the WebDriver session.

Q7: How do you open a new tab in Selenium 4?

A: driver.switchTo().newWindow(WindowType.TAB) then navigate with driver.get().

Q8: How do you switch to a newly opened window?

A: Store the parent handle, wait for numberOfWindowsToBe(2), iterate getWindowHandles(), switch to the handle that is not the parent.

Q9: What happens if you try to find an element inside a frame without switching?

A: Selenium throws NoSuchElementException because it searches the current context (main page), not the frame content.

Q10: How do you wait for a frame to load before switching?

A: wait.until(ExpectedConditions.frameToBeAvailableAndSwitchToIt("frame-id"))

Q11: Can a page have multiple frames?

A: Yes. Use index, name/id, or WebElement to switch to the specific frame you need. Always switch back to defaultContent when done.

Q12: How do you close all popup windows and return to the main window?

A: Store main handle, iterate all handles, close each non-main window, then switchTo().window(mainHandle).

Q13: What is NoSuchWindowException?

A: Thrown when trying to switch to a window handle that no longer exists (already closed) or is invalid.

Q14: How do you get the total number of open windows?

A: driver.getWindowHandles().size()

Section 23: Actions Class

What Is the Actions Class?

The Actions class in Selenium WebDriver provides a low-level, user-like way to perform advanced interactions that go beyond simple element.click() or sendKeys(). It simulates real mouse movements, keyboard input, and composite gestures — hover menus, drag-and-drop, sliders, right-click context menus, and multi-key combinations.

Key idea: Actions builds a queue of interaction steps. Nothing happens until you call .perform() (or .build().perform()).

Creating an Actions Object

import org.openqa.selenium.interactions.Actions;

Actions actions = new Actions(driver);

Mouse Actions

moveToElement() — Hover

Syntax: actions.moveToElement(element).perform();

WebElement menu = driver.findElement(By.id("products-menu"));
actions.moveToElement(menu).perform();

Real scenario: Hover over a navigation menu item so a submenu appears, then click a submenu link.

click() — Alternative Click

Syntax: actions.click(element).perform();

WebElement submitBtn = driver.findElement(By.id("submit"));
actions.click(submitBtn).perform();

Real scenario: Use when a standard click is intercepted by an overlay or another element.

doubleClick()

Syntax: actions.doubleClick(element).perform();

WebElement fileItem = driver.findElement(By.xpath("//span[text()='report.pdf']"));
actions.doubleClick(fileItem).perform();

Real scenario: Open a file in a file manager, or select a word in a text editor.

contextClick() — Right-Click

Syntax: actions.contextClick(element).perform();

WebElement row = driver.findElement(By.xpath("//tr[td='John Doe']"));
actions.contextClick(row).perform();

Real scenario: Open a context menu to copy, delete, or edit a table row.

clickAndHold() + release() — Slider / Drag

Syntax:

actions.clickAndHold(slider).moveByOffset(200, 0).release().perform();

Real scenario: Drag a price-range slider or resize a panel.

dragAndDrop(source, target)

Syntax: actions.dragAndDrop(source, target).perform();

WebElement source = driver.findElement(By.id("task-1"));
WebElement target = driver.findElement(By.id("done-column"));
actions.dragAndDrop(source, target).perform();

Real scenario: Move a Kanban card from "To Do" to "Done".

dragAndDropBy(source, xOffset, yOffset)

Syntax: actions.dragAndDropBy(source, xOffset, yOffset).perform();

WebElement handle = driver.findElement(By.className("slider-handle"));
actions.dragAndDropBy(handle, 150, 0).perform();

Real scenario: Pixel-precise drag when there is no explicit drop target element.

Keyboard Actions

sendKeys(Keys.ENTER) — Submit Form

WebElement searchBox = driver.findElement(By.name("q"));
actions.sendKeys(searchBox, "Selenium").sendKeys(Keys.ENTER).perform();

keyDown + click + keyUp — Multi-Select

WebElement item1 = driver.findElement(By.id("item-1"));
WebElement item2 = driver.findElement(By.id("item-2"));
actions.keyDown(Keys.CONTROL).click(item1).click(item2).keyUp(Keys.CONTROL).perform();

sendKeys(Keys.chord(...)) — Select All

WebElement textArea = driver.findElement(By.id("editor"));
actions.click(textArea).sendKeys(Keys.chord(Keys.CONTROL, "a")).perform();

Common Keys: TAB, ESCAPE, ARROW_DOWN

actions.sendKeys(Keys.TAB).perform();           // move focus
actions.sendKeys(Keys.ESCAPE).perform();        // close modal
actions.sendKeys(Keys.ARROW_DOWN).perform();    // navigate dropdown

Action Chains

Chain multiple steps into one user flow:

WebElement menu    = driver.findElement(By.id("products"));
WebElement submenu = driver.findElement(By.linkText("Laptops"));

actions.moveToElement(menu).click(submenu).perform();
Critical: You MUST call .perform() or .build().perform(). Without it, the queued actions never execute.

Selenium 4 New Scroll Actions

// Scroll element into view
actions.scrollToElement(element).perform();

// Scroll by pixel amount (x, y)
actions.scrollByAmount(0, 500).perform();

Complete Example — Menu Hover, Drag-Drop, Slider, Right-Click

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.interactions.Actions;
import java.time.Duration;

public class ActionsDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();
        driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(Duration.ofSeconds(10));
        driver.get("https://example.com/app");
        Actions actions = new Actions(driver);

        // 1. Hover menu → click submenu
        WebElement menu = driver.findElement(By.id("nav-products"));
        WebElement submenu = driver.findElement(By.linkText("Electronics"));
        actions.moveToElement(menu).pause(Duration.ofMillis(500))
               .click(submenu).perform();

        // 2. Drag and drop
        WebElement source = driver.findElement(By.id("drag-item"));
        WebElement target = driver.findElement(By.id("drop-zone"));
        actions.dragAndDrop(source, target).perform();

        // 3. Slider via clickAndHold
        WebElement slider = driver.findElement(By.className("slider-thumb"));
        actions.clickAndHold(slider).moveByOffset(200, 0).release().perform();

        // 4. Right-click context menu
        WebElement row = driver.findElement(By.xpath("//tr[td='Invoice-101']"));
        actions.contextClick(row).perform();

        driver.quit();
    }
}

Interview Q&A (10+)

#QuestionAnswer
1What is the Actions class?A Selenium API for advanced user interactions — mouse, keyboard, and composite gestures.
2Why must you call perform()?Actions queues steps; perform() executes the entire chain in one atomic user gesture.
3Difference between click() and Actions click()?Actions click moves the mouse to the element first; useful when elements need focus or hover state.
4How do you hover over an element?actions.moveToElement(element).perform();
5How to perform drag and drop?actions.dragAndDrop(source, target).perform();
6dragAndDrop vs dragAndDropBy?dragAndDrop needs a target element; dragAndDropBy moves by pixel offset from source.
7How to multi-select with keyboard?keyDown(CONTROL).click(...).click(...).keyUp(CONTROL).perform()
8What is Keys.chord()?Combines multiple keys into one sendKeys call, e.g. Ctrl+A.
9Can Actions handle iframes?You must switch to the iframe first; Actions operates on the current browsing context.
10Selenium 4 scroll actions?scrollToElement() and scrollByAmount(x, y) replace many JS scroll hacks.
11build() vs perform()?build() returns Action object for reuse; perform() executes immediately (internally calls build().perform()).
12When does Actions fail?Element not visible, out of viewport, covered by overlay, or stale reference.

Section 24: JavaScript Executor

What Is JavascriptExecutor?

JavascriptExecutor is a Selenium interface that lets you execute JavaScript directly in the browser's context. Use it when standard WebDriver commands cannot interact with an element — hidden inputs, read-only fields, elements blocked by overlays, or custom widgets.

Casting the Driver

JavascriptExecutor js = (JavascriptExecutor) driver;

Common Operations

Click Element (when regular click fails)

WebElement btn = driver.findElement(By.id("hidden-submit"));
js.executeScript("arguments[0].click();", btn);

Scroll to Element

WebElement footer = driver.findElement(By.id("footer"));
js.executeScript("arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", footer);

Scroll to Bottom of Page

js.executeScript("window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight)");

Scroll by Pixels

js.executeScript("window.scrollBy(0, 500)");

Highlight Element (debugging)

js.executeScript("arguments[0].style.border='3px solid red'", element);

Get Text from Element

String text = (String) js.executeScript("return arguments[0].innerText", element);

Set Value (hidden inputs, read-only fields)

js.executeScript("arguments[0].value='admin@example.com'", element);

Get Page Title

String title = (String) js.executeScript("return document.title");

Get Domain

String domain = (String) js.executeScript("return document.domain");

Remove Attribute (e.g., readonly)

js.executeScript("arguments[0].removeAttribute('readonly')", dateField);

Trigger Change Event (after setting value)

js.executeScript(
    "arguments[0].value='2026-07-14';" +
    "arguments[0].dispatchEvent(new Event('change', { bubbles: true }));",
    dateField
);

When to Use JSExecutor vs Regular Selenium

ScenarioRegular SeleniumJavascriptExecutor
Visible button clickPreferredOverkill
Element covered by overlayMay failJS click works
Hidden / disabled inputCannot typeSet value via JS
Read-only date pickerBlockedRemove attribute + set value
Scroll into viewActions / nativescrollIntoView reliable
User-like interaction testingPreferred (realistic)Bypasses UI events
Get computed stylesLimitedFull DOM access
Async page logicWaitsexecuteAsyncScript

executeAsyncScript — Async Operations

Use when JavaScript returns a result after a delay (AJAX, setTimeout):

Long result = (Long) js.executeAsyncScript(
    "var callback = arguments[arguments.length - 1];" +
    "setTimeout(function(){ callback(document.querySelectorAll('li').length); }, 2000);"
);
System.out.println("List items: " + result);
Rule of thumb: Prefer regular Selenium for user-facing tests. Use JSExecutor as a fallback or for DOM manipulation that WebDriver cannot reach.

Interview Q&A (10+)

#QuestionAnswer
1What is JavascriptExecutor?Selenium interface to run JS in the browser context via the driver.
2How do you cast the driver?JavascriptExecutor js = (JavascriptExecutor) driver;
3Why use JS click?When element is not clickable (overlay, off-screen, display:none parent).
4What is arguments[0]?First parameter passed from Java to the JS script — typically a WebElement.
5executeScript vs executeAsyncScript?Sync returns immediately; async waits for a callback before returning.
6Can JSExecutor work in all browsers?Yes — all WebDriver implementations support it.
7Downside of JS click?Skips real user events; may miss bugs in click handlers.
8How to scroll to bottom?window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight)
9How to set readonly field value?Remove readonly attribute, set value, dispatch change event.
10Return types from executeScript?String, Long, Boolean, WebElement, List, or null — cast appropriately.
11Does JSExecutor work in iframes?Only after switching to the iframe context.
12Is JSExecutor cross-browser?Yes, but JS DOM APIs must be supported by the target browser.

Section 25: Web Tables

Static vs Dynamic Tables

Static tables have a fixed number of rows and columns defined in HTML. Dynamic tables load data from a server via AJAX; row count varies and pagination may apply.

Table HTML Structure

<table>
  <thead>
    <tr><th>Name</th><th>Role</th><th>Action</th></tr>
  </thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr><td>Alice</td><td>Admin</td><td><button>Edit</button></td></tr>
    <tr><td>Bob</td><td>User</td><td><button>Edit</button></td></tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

Common Table Operations

Get Row Count

int rowCount = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr")).size();

Get Column Count

int colCount = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table//thead/tr/th")).size();

Get Cell Value (row, col — 1-based)

String cell = driver.findElement(
    By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr[2]/td[3]")
).getText();

Get Entire Row

WebElement row = driver.findElement(By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr[1]"));
List<WebElement> cells = row.findElements(By.tagName("td"));
for (WebElement cell : cells) {
    System.out.println(cell.getText());
}

Search for Value in Table

List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr"));
for (int i = 0; i < rows.size(); i++) {
    if (rows.get(i).getText().contains("Alice")) {
        System.out.println("Found at row: " + (i + 1));
    }
}

Click Action in Specific Row

// Find row by text, click button in same row
WebElement row = driver.findElement(By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr[td='Alice']"));
row.findElement(By.tagName("button")).click();

Complete Utility Class — WebTableUtils

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.ExpectedConditions;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.WebDriverWait;
import java.time.Duration;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.List;

public class WebTableUtils {
    private WebDriver driver;
    private WebDriverWait wait;
    private static final String TABLE_XPATH = "//table[@id='data-table']";

    public WebTableUtils(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    public int getRowCount() {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.presenceOfElementLocated(By.xpath(TABLE_XPATH)));
        return driver.findElements(By.xpath(TABLE_XPATH + "//tbody/tr")).size();
    }

    public int getColumnCount() {
        return driver.findElements(By.xpath(TABLE_XPATH + "//thead/tr/th")).size();
    }

    public String getCellValue(int row, int col) {
        String xpath = TABLE_XPATH + "//tbody/tr[" + row + "]/td[" + col + "]";
        return driver.findElement(By.xpath(xpath)).getText().trim();
    }

    public List<String> getColumnData(int colIndex) {
        List<String> columnData = new ArrayList<>();
        int rows = getRowCount();
        for (int i = 1; i <= rows; i++) {
            columnData.add(getCellValue(i, colIndex));
        }
        return columnData;
    }

    public int searchTable(String searchText) {
        List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.xpath(TABLE_XPATH + "//tbody/tr"));
        for (int i = 0; i < rows.size(); i++) {
            if (rows.get(i).getText().contains(searchText)) {
                return i + 1; // 1-based row number
            }
        }
        return -1;
    }

    public void clickActionInRow(String searchText, int actionColIndex) {
        int rowNum = searchTable(searchText);
        if (rowNum == -1) throw new NoSuchElementException("Row not found: " + searchText);
        String xpath = TABLE_XPATH + "//tbody/tr[" + rowNum + "]/td[" + actionColIndex + "]//button";
        driver.findElement(By.xpath(xpath)).click();
    }
}

Pagination Handling

while (true) {
    // process current page rows
    List<WebElement> rows = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//table//tbody/tr"));
    for (WebElement row : rows) { /* read data */ }

    List<WebElement> nextBtn = driver.findElements(By.xpath("//a[text()='Next']"));
    if (nextBtn.isEmpty() || nextBtn.get(0).getAttribute("class").contains("disabled")) break;
    nextBtn.get(0).click();
}

Sorting Validation

WebTableUtils table = new WebTableUtils(driver);
List<String> names = table.getColumnData(1);
List<String> sorted = new ArrayList<>(names);
sorted.sort(String.CASE_INSENSITIVE_ORDER);
Assert.assertEquals(names, sorted, "Column is not sorted A-Z");

Real Examples

Employee Table

// Verify employee "John Doe" has role "Manager"
int row = table.searchTable("John Doe");
Assert.assertEquals(table.getCellValue(row, 2), "Manager");

Order Table

// Click "View" for order ORD-9876
table.clickActionInRow("ORD-9876", 5);

Interview Q&A (10+)

#QuestionAnswer
1Static vs dynamic table?Static: fixed HTML rows. Dynamic: AJAX-loaded, row count changes.
2XPath for row count?//table//tbody/tr — use findElements().size()
3How to get cell by row/col?//table//tbody/tr[row]/td[col] (1-based index)
4How to click button in a row?Find row by text, then find button within that row element.
5Are row indexes 0-based in XPath?No — XPath indexes are 1-based.
6How to handle pagination?Loop pages, process rows, click Next until disabled or absent.
7How to validate sorting?Extract column data into List, compare with sorted copy.
8Nested tables?Use more specific XPath; scope search within parent table element.
9Table without thead?Use first tbody row for column count or known structure.
10Best locator strategy for tables?Relative XPath from table id; avoid absolute paths.
11How to wait for dynamic table?WebDriverWait for row presence or expected row count.
12Can we use CSS for tables?Yes, but XPath is more natural for row/column indexing.

Section 26: Screenshot Capture

TakesScreenshot Interface

Selenium captures screenshots via the TakesScreenshot interface. Cast the driver and save the output as a file, bytes, or Base64.

import org.openqa.selenium.OutputType;
import org.openqa.selenium.TakesScreenshot;
import java.io.File;
import org.apache.commons.io.FileUtils;

File screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
FileUtils.copyFile(screenshot, new File("screenshot.png"));

Full Page Screenshot

public static void captureFullPage(WebDriver driver, String path) throws IOException {
    File src = ((TakesScreenshot) driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
    FileUtils.copyFile(src, new File(path));
}

Element Screenshot (Selenium 4)

Selenium 4 allows screenshots directly on a WebElement:

WebElement element = driver.findElement(By.id("chart-panel"));
File elementShot = element.getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
FileUtils.copyFile(elementShot, new File("chart.png"));

Screenshot Utility Class

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.apache.commons.io.FileUtils;
import java.io.File;
import java.io.IOException;
import java.time.LocalDateTime;
import java.time.format.DateTimeFormatter;

public class ScreenshotUtils {
    private static final String BASE_DIR = "screenshots/";

    public static String capture(WebDriver driver, String testName) {
        String timestamp = LocalDateTime.now()
            .format(DateTimeFormatter.ofPattern("yyyyMMdd_HHmmss"));
        String folder = BASE_DIR + testName + "/";
        new File(folder).mkdirs();
        String filePath = folder + testName + "_" + timestamp + ".png";

        try {
            File src = ((TakesScreenshot) driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
            FileUtils.copyFile(src, new File(filePath));
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Screenshot failed: " + e.getMessage());
        }
        return filePath;
    }

    public static String captureElement(WebElement element, String testName) {
        String timestamp = LocalDateTime.now()
            .format(DateTimeFormatter.ofPattern("yyyyMMdd_HHmmss"));
        String filePath = BASE_DIR + testName + "/element_" + timestamp + ".png";
        new File(BASE_DIR + testName + "/").mkdirs();
        try {
            File src = element.getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
            FileUtils.copyFile(src, new File(filePath));
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Element screenshot failed", e);
        }
        return filePath;
    }
}

TestNG Listener — Screenshot on Failure

import org.testng.ITestListener;
import org.testng.ITestResult;

public class ScreenshotListener implements ITestListener {
    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        WebDriver driver = (WebDriver) result.getTestContext()
            .getAttribute("driver");
        if (driver != null) {
            String path = ScreenshotUtils.capture(driver, result.getName());
            result.setAttribute("screenshot", path);
            System.out.println("Screenshot saved: " + path);
        }
    }
}

Cucumber Integration — Scenario.attach()

import io.cucumber.java.After;
import io.cucumber.java.Scenario;
import org.openqa.selenium.OutputType;
import org.openqa.selenium.TakesScreenshot;

public class Hooks {
    @After
    public void afterScenario(Scenario scenario) {
        if (scenario.isFailed()) {
            byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
                .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
            scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", "Failure Screenshot");
        }
    }
}

Extent Reports Integration

// Inside TestListener onTestFailure
String path = ScreenshotUtils.capture(driver, result.getName());
test.addScreenCaptureFromPath(path);

Ashot Library — Full Page with Scrolling

// Maven: ru.yandex.qatools.ashot:ashot
import ru.yandex.qatools.ashot.AShot;
import ru.yandex.qatools.ashot.shooting.ShootingStrategies;
import javax.imageio.ImageIO;
import java.io.File;

public static void fullPageAshot(WebDriver driver, String path) throws Exception {
    BufferedImage image = new AShot()
        .shootingStrategy(ShootingStrategies.viewportPasting(1000))
        .takeScreenshot(driver);
    ImageIO.write(image, "PNG", new File(path));
}
Best practice: Capture screenshots on failure only in CI to save disk space. Use timestamped folders per test for easy debugging.

Interview Q&A (8+)

#QuestionAnswer
1How to take a screenshot in Selenium?Cast driver to TakesScreenshot, call getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE).
2OutputType options?FILE, BYTES, BASE64 — choose based on storage or reporting needs.
3Element screenshot in Selenium 4?element.getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE) — no third-party lib needed.
4When to capture screenshots?On test failure, critical checkpoints, or visual regression.
5TestNG listener for screenshots?Implement ITestListener.onTestFailure(), capture and attach path.
6Cucumber screenshot attach?scenario.attach(bytes, "image/png", "name") in @After hook.
7Why use Ashot?Captures full scrollable page; native screenshot is viewport-only.
8Does TakesScreenshot work on RemoteWebDriver?Yes — works with Grid and cloud providers.
9Headless screenshot?Yes — headless browsers support TakesScreenshot normally.

Section 27: Page Object Model (POM)

What Is POM?

The Page Object Model is a design pattern that separates page structure (locators and UI actions) from test logic (assertions and workflows). Each web page gets a dedicated Java class encapsulating its elements and interactions.

Why POM?

  • Maintainability: Locator changes happen in one place.
  • Reusability: Page methods shared across multiple tests.
  • Readability: Tests read like business scenarios.

POM Architecture

┌─────────────┐     calls      ┌──────────────┐     uses     ┌────────────┐     drives    ┌──────────┐
│  Test Class │ ──────────────▶│  Page Object │ ───────────▶│ WebElement │ ────────────▶│   Page   │
│ LoginTest   │                │  LoginPage   │             │  locators  │             │ Browser  │
└─────────────┘                └──────────────┘             └────────────┘             └──────────┘

POM Rules

  1. One page class per web page (or major view).
  2. All locators live inside the page class — never in tests.
  3. All page interactions are exposed as methods.
  4. Return type: next page object (navigation) or void (action).
  5. No assertions inside page objects — tests assert outcomes.

Without POM vs With POM

Without POM (anti-pattern)

@Test
public void loginTest() {
    driver.findElement(By.id("username")).sendKeys("admin");
    driver.findElement(By.id("password")).sendKeys("pass123");
    driver.findElement(By.id("loginBtn")).click();
    Assert.assertEquals(driver.getTitle(), "Home");
}

With POM (recommended)

@Test
public void loginTest() {
    HomePage home = new LoginPage(driver)
        .enterUsername("admin")
        .enterPassword("pass123")
        .clickLogin();
    Assert.assertTrue(home.verifyHomePage());
}

Complete POM Example

LoginPage.java

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.FindBy;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.PageFactory;

public class LoginPage {
    private WebDriver driver;

    @FindBy(id = "username") private WebElement usernameField;
    @FindBy(id = "password") private WebElement passwordField;
    @FindBy(id = "loginBtn")  private WebElement loginButton;

    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    public LoginPage enterUsername(String username) {
        usernameField.clear();
        usernameField.sendKeys(username);
        return this;
    }

    public LoginPage enterPassword(String password) {
        passwordField.clear();
        passwordField.sendKeys(password);
        return this;
    }

    public HomePage clickLogin() {
        loginButton.click();
        return new HomePage(driver);
    }

    public void login(String user, String pass) {
        enterUsername(user).enterPassword(pass).clickLogin();
    }
}

HomePage.java

public class HomePage {
    private WebDriver driver;

    @FindBy(className = "welcome-msg") private WebElement welcomeText;
    @FindBy(id = "dashboard")         private WebElement dashboard;

    public HomePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    public boolean verifyHomePage() {
        return dashboard.isDisplayed();
    }

    public String getWelcomeText() {
        return welcomeText.getText();
    }
}

LoginTest.java

import org.testng.Assert;
import org.testng.annotations.Test;

public class LoginTest extends BaseTest {
    @Test
    public void validLogin() {
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);
        HomePage home = loginPage
            .enterUsername("admin")
            .enterPassword("pass123")
            .clickLogin();
        Assert.assertTrue(home.verifyHomePage());
        Assert.assertEquals(home.getWelcomeText(), "Welcome, admin!");
    }
}

Method Chaining (Fluent Interface)

loginPage.enterUsername("admin").enterPassword("pass").clickLogin();

Each method returns this (same page) or the next page object (navigation), enabling readable fluent chains.

POM for Complex Pages — Components

public class DashboardPage {
