    private HeaderComponent header;
    private SidebarComponent sidebar;

    public DashboardPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.header  = new HeaderComponent(driver);
        this.sidebar = new SidebarComponent(driver);
    }

    public HeaderComponent getHeader() { return header; }
    public SidebarComponent getSidebar() { return sidebar; }
}

POM Best Practices (10 Points)

  1. One class per page or major UI section.
  2. Use meaningful method names reflecting user actions.
  3. Keep locators private; expose behavior, not elements.
  4. Return next page object after navigation.
  5. Never put assertions in page classes.
  6. Extend a BasePage for shared waits and utilities.
  7. Avoid hardcoded test data — pass via method parameters.
  8. Split large pages into component classes.
  9. Use explicit waits inside page methods.
  10. Keep page objects free of TestNG/JUnit annotations.

POM Anti-Patterns

Anti-PatternProblemFix
God Page ObjectOne class for entire appSplit by page/component
Assertions in pagesMixes UI logic with test logicAssert only in test classes
Hardcoded dataNot reusable across testsParameterize methods
Public WebElementsTests bypass page methodsKeep elements private
Driver in testsTests interact with DOM directlyAll interaction via page objects

Interview Q&A (12+)

#QuestionAnswer
1What is POM?Design pattern separating page locators/actions from test logic.
2Why use POM?Maintainability, reusability, readability, reduced duplication.
3Can page objects contain assertions?No — assertions belong in test classes.
4What should a page method return?Next page object after navigation, or this/void for actions.
5What is method chaining?Fluent interface — methods return this or next page for chaining.
6One page class per what?Per web page or distinct UI view/section.
7What is a God Page Object?Anti-pattern: one massive class handling entire application.
8How to handle shared headers/footers?Extract into reusable component classes.
9POM vs PageFactory?POM is the pattern; PageFactory is an implementation using @FindBy.
10Where do waits go?Inside page methods or BasePage — not scattered in tests.
11Should tests access WebElements?No — always go through page object methods.
12How does POM help maintenance?Locator change in one file updates all tests using that page.

Section 28: Page Factory

What Is Page Factory?

Page Factory is Selenium's built-in implementation of POM using @FindBy annotations. It initializes WebElements lazily via PageFactory.initElements(), reducing boilerplate locator code.

@FindBy Annotation

@FindBy(id = "email")
WebElement emailField;

Other @FindBy Locator Strategies

StrategyExample
id@FindBy(id = "submit")
name@FindBy(name = "username")
className@FindBy(className = "btn-primary")
css@FindBy(css = "input[type='email']")
xpath@FindBy(xpath = "//button[text()='Login']")
linkText@FindBy(linkText = "Forgot Password")
partialLinkText@FindBy(partialLinkText = "Forgot")
tagName@FindBy(tagName = "textarea")

@FindBys — AND Condition

All locators must match (element must satisfy every condition):

@FindBys({
    @FindBy(id = "login-form"),
    @FindBy(tagName = "input")
})
WebElement usernameInForm;

@FindAll — OR Condition

Any locator match returns the element:

@FindAll({
    @FindBy(id = "submit-btn"),
    @FindBy(css = "button[type='submit']")
})
WebElement submitButton;

initElements

public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
    this.driver = driver;
    PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
}

Call in the constructor (or @BeforeMethod) to bind annotated fields to live WebElements.

@CacheLookup

@CacheLookup
@FindBy(id = "app-logo")
WebElement logo;
Warning: Use @CacheLookup only for static elements that never change. Dynamic elements cause StaleElementReferenceException.

Complete PageFactory Example

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.FindBy;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.PageFactory;

public class LoginPage {
    private WebDriver driver;

    @FindBy(id = "username")   private WebElement usernameField;
    @FindBy(id = "password")   private WebElement passwordField;
    @FindBy(id = "loginBtn")    private WebElement loginButton;
    @FindBy(className = "error") private WebElement errorMessage;

    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    public void enterUsername(String username) {
        usernameField.clear();
        usernameField.sendKeys(username);
    }

    public void enterPassword(String password) {
        passwordField.sendKeys(password);
    }

    public HomePage clickLogin() {
        loginButton.click();
        return new HomePage(driver);
    }

    public String getErrorMessage() {
        return errorMessage.getText();
    }
}

POM vs PageFactory Comparison

AspectManual POMPageFactory
Locator declarationBy.id("email") in code@FindBy(id="email") annotation
Element initializationfindElement() each callLazy init via initElements()
BoilerplateMore verboseLess verbose
Dynamic locatorsFull supportNot supported natively
CachingManual@CacheLookup built-in
Stale element riskLower (re-find each time)Higher with @CacheLookup

PageFactory Limitations

  • StaleElementReferenceException with @CacheLookup on dynamic/AJAX elements.
  • No dynamic locators — cannot parameterize @FindBy at runtime.
  • Deprecation discussion — Selenium team has discussed deprecating PageFactory; manual POM remains fully supported.

When to Use POM vs PageFactory

CriteriaManual POMPageFactory
Dynamic/AJAX pagesPreferredUse cautiously
Static formsEitherPageFactory is fine
Parameterized locatorsManual POMNot suitable
Large team, annotationsEitherPageFactory readable
Long-term Selenium 4+Manual POM saferMonitor deprecation

Interview Q&A (10+)

#QuestionAnswer
1What is Page Factory?Selenium's @FindBy-based POM implementation with initElements().
2What does initElements do?Scans @FindBy fields and creates lazy WebElement proxies.
3@FindBys vs @FindAll?@FindBys = AND (all match); @FindAll = OR (any match).
4What is @CacheLookup?Caches element reference after first find — static elements only.
5When does @CacheLookup fail?When DOM refreshes and cached reference becomes stale.
6Can @FindBy use XPath?Yes — @FindBy(xpath = "...")
7PageFactory vs manual POM?PageFactory uses annotations; manual POM uses By locators in code.
8Is PageFactory deprecated?Discussed for deprecation; check current Selenium release notes.
9Dynamic locator with PageFactory?Not supported — use manual findElement with parameters.
10Where to call initElements?Page object constructor or test setup before interaction.
11Are PageFactory elements lazy?Yes — located on first use, not at initElements time.
12Can private fields use @FindBy?Yes — recommended to encapsulate elements.

Section 29: Hybrid Automation Framework

What Is a Hybrid Framework?

A Hybrid Framework combines multiple automation approaches: POM for page structure, Data-Driven testing via Excel/JSON, Keyword-Driven reusable actions, and TestNG for execution, reporting, and parallel runs.

Framework Design Principles

  • DRY — Don't Repeat Yourself; shared utilities in one place.
  • SRP — Single Responsibility; each class has one job.
  • OCP — Open/Closed; extend via new pages/tests without modifying core.
  • Loose coupling — Tests depend on page interfaces, not driver details.
  • High cohesion — Related logic grouped (pages, utils, config).

1. DriverManager.java

package com.framework.driver;

import com.framework.enums.BrowserType;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;

public class DriverManager {
    private static ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driver = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static WebDriver getDriver() {
        return driver.get();
    }

    public static void setDriver(BrowserType browser) {
        driver.set(DriverFactory.createDriver(browser));
    }

    public static void quitDriver() {
        if (driver.get() != null) {
            driver.get().quit();
            driver.remove();
        }
    }
}

2. ConfigReader.java

package com.framework.config;

import java.io.IOException;
import java.io.InputStream;
import java.util.Properties;

public class ConfigReader {
    private static ConfigReader instance;
    private Properties properties = new Properties();

    private ConfigReader() {
        try (InputStream is = getClass().getClassLoader()
                .getResourceAsStream("config.properties")) {
            properties.load(is);
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to load config.properties", e);
        }
    }

    public static synchronized ConfigReader getInstance() {
        if (instance == null) instance = new ConfigReader();
        return instance;
    }

    public String get(String key) {
        return properties.getProperty(key);
    }

    public int getInt(String key) {
        return Integer.parseInt(properties.getProperty(key));
    }
}

3. BasePage.java

package com.framework.base;

import com.framework.driver.DriverManager;
import com.framework.utils.WaitUtils;
import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.interactions.Actions;

public class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WaitUtils waitUtils;

    public BasePage() {
        this.driver = DriverManager.getDriver();
        this.waitUtils = new WaitUtils(driver);
    }

    protected void click(WebElement element) {
        waitUtils.waitForClickable(element);
        element.click();
    }

    protected void type(WebElement element, String text) {
        waitUtils.waitForVisible(element);
        element.clear();
        element.sendKeys(text);
    }

    protected void scrollTo(WebElement element) {
        new Actions(driver).scrollToElement(element).perform();
    }

    protected String getText(WebElement element) {
        waitUtils.waitForVisible(element);
        return element.getText();
    }
}

4. BaseTest.java

package com.framework.base;

import com.framework.config.ConfigReader;
import com.framework.driver.DriverManager;
import com.framework.enums.BrowserType;
import com.framework.reports.ExtentReportManager;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.testng.annotations.*;

public class BaseTest {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected ConfigReader config = ConfigReader.getInstance();

    @BeforeSuite
    public void initReports() {
        ExtentReportManager.initReport();
    }

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setUp() {
        BrowserType browser = BrowserType.valueOf(config.get("browser").toUpperCase());
        DriverManager.setDriver(browser);
        driver = DriverManager.getDriver();
        driver.manage().window().maximize();
        driver.get(config.get("url"));
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void tearDown() {
        DriverManager.quitDriver();
    }

    @AfterSuite
    public void flushReports() {
        ExtentReportManager.flushReport();
    }
}

5. LoginPage.java

package com.framework.pages;

import com.framework.base.BasePage;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.FindBy;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.PageFactory;

public class LoginPage extends BasePage {

    @FindBy(id = "username") private WebElement usernameField;
    @FindBy(id = "password") private WebElement passwordField;
    @FindBy(id = "loginBtn")  private WebElement loginButton;
    @FindBy(className = "error-msg") private WebElement errorMsg;

    public LoginPage() {
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    public LoginPage enterUsername(String username) {
        type(usernameField, username);
        return this;
    }

    public LoginPage enterPassword(String password) {
        type(passwordField, password);
        return this;
    }

    public HomePage clickLogin() {
        click(loginButton);
        return new HomePage();
    }

    public HomePage login(String user, String pass) {
        return enterUsername(user).enterPassword(pass).clickLogin();
    }

    public String getErrorMessage() {
        return getText(errorMsg);
    }
}

6. LoginTest.java

package com.framework.tests;

import com.framework.base.BaseTest;
import com.framework.pages.HomePage;
import com.framework.pages.LoginPage;
import org.testng.Assert;
import org.testng.annotations.Test;

public class LoginTest extends BaseTest {

    @Test(dataProvider = "loginData", dataProviderClass = LoginDataProvider.class,
          groups = {"smoke"})
    public void testLogin(String username, String password, boolean expectedSuccess) {
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage();
        if (expectedSuccess) {
            HomePage home = loginPage.login(username, password);
            Assert.assertTrue(home.isDashboardDisplayed());
        } else {
            loginPage.login(username, password);
            Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getErrorMessage().contains("Invalid"));
        }
    }
}

7. TestListener.java

package com.framework.listeners;

import com.framework.driver.DriverManager;
import com.framework.reports.ExtentReportManager;
import com.framework.utils.ScreenshotUtils;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentTest;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.testng.ITestListener;
import org.testng.ITestResult;

public class TestListener implements ITestListener {
    @Override
    public void onTestStart(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentReportManager.createTest(result.getMethod().getMethodName());
    }

    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        WebDriver driver = DriverManager.getDriver();
        ExtentTest test = ExtentReportManager.getTest();
        if (driver != null) {
            String path = ScreenshotUtils.capture(driver, result.getName());
            test.addScreenCaptureFromPath(path);
            test.fail(result.getThrowable());
        }
    }

    @Override
    public void onTestSuccess(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentReportManager.getTest().pass("Test passed");
    }
}

Design Patterns Used

PatternWhereWhy

SingletonConfigReader, ExtentReportManagerSingle config/report instance

Interview Q&A (12+)

#QuestionAnswer
1What is a Hybrid Framework?Combines POM, Data-Driven, Keyword-Driven, and TestNG.
2Why ThreadLocal for WebDriver?Each parallel thread gets its own driver instance safely.
3Role of BasePage?Shared actions: click, type, wait, scroll for all pages.
4Role of BaseTest?Setup/teardown, driver init, report lifecycle.
5Why ConfigReader singleton?Load properties once, access globally.
6What is DriverFactory?Creates Chrome/Firefox/Edge WebDriver based on config.
7How does data-driven work?@DataProvider reads Excel, feeds rows to @Test method.
8Where do screenshots go on failure?TestListener captures and attaches to Extent Report.
9DRY in framework context?Reusable utils — no duplicate wait/click code in tests.
10smoke.xml purpose?Run smoke group tests with parallel execution config.
11How to add a new page?Create page class extending BasePage, add to tests.
12Loose coupling example?Tests use LoginPage methods, not raw findElement calls.

Section 30: Selenium + TestNG Integration

Why TestNG with Selenium?

  • Annotations — structured test lifecycle (@BeforeMethod, @Test, etc.).
  • Parallel execution — run tests concurrently via testng.xml.
  • Grouping — smoke, regression, sanity test suites.
  • Data-driven — @DataProvider feeds multiple datasets to one test.
  • Reporting — listeners, HTML reports, Extent integration.

Annotations Mapping to Selenium Lifecycle

AnnotationSelenium Action
@BeforeSuiteInitialize reports, load global config
@BeforeTestLoad environment-specific config
@BeforeClassLaunch browser (or per-method in BaseTest)
@BeforeMethodNavigate to base URL, start test timer
@TestExecute automation steps via page objects
@AfterMethodScreenshot on failure, logout, close tabs
@AfterClassClose browser session
@AfterSuiteFlush reports, cleanup temp files

DataProvider with Selenium — Excel DataProvider

import com.framework.utils.ExcelUtils;
import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;

public class LoginDataProvider {

    @DataProvider(name = "loginData")
    public Object[][] getLoginData() {
        ExcelUtils excel = new ExcelUtils("src/test/resources/testdata/loginData.xlsx");
        int rows = excel.getRowCount("Login");
        Object[][] data = new Object[rows - 1][3];
        for (int i = 1; i < rows; i++) {
            data[i - 1][0] = excel.getCellData("Login", i, 0); // username
            data[i - 1][1] = excel.getCellData("Login", i, 1); // password
            data[i - 1][2] = Boolean.parseBoolean(excel.getCellData("Login", i, 2));
        }
        return data;
    }
}

Multiple Data Sets for Login Testing

@DataProvider(name = "loginScenarios")
public Object[][] loginScenarios() {
    return new Object[][] {
        {"admin",   "admin123",  true},
        {"guest",   "guest123",  true},
        {"invalid", "wrong",     false},
        {"",        "pass",      false},
        {"admin",   "",          false}
    };
}

Assertions in Selenium

Hard Assertions

// Stops test immediately on failure
Assert.assertEquals(driver.getTitle(), "Dashboard");
Assert.assertTrue(driver.getCurrentUrl().contains("/home"));
Assert.assertEquals(element.getText(), "Welcome, admin!");

Soft Assertions

import org.testng.asserts.SoftAssert;

SoftAssert soft = new SoftAssert();
soft.assertEquals(header.getText(), "Dashboard");
soft.assertTrue(footer.isDisplayed());
soft.assertEquals(sidebar.getMenuCount(), 5);
soft.assertAll(); // report all failures at end

Parallel Execution

<!DOCTYPE suite SYSTEM "https://testng.org/testng-1.0.dtd">
<suite name="Parallel Suite" parallel="tests" thread-count="3">
  <test name="Chrome Tests">
    <parameter name="browser" value="chrome"/>
    <classes><class name="com.framework.tests.LoginTest"/></classes>
  </test>
  <test name="Firefox Tests">
    <parameter name="browser" value="firefox"/>
    <classes><class name="com.framework.tests.LoginTest"/></classes>
  </test>
</suite>
Essential: Use ThreadLocal<WebDriver> in DriverManager — without it, parallel tests share one driver and fail unpredictably.

Cross-Browser Parallel Example

@BeforeMethod
@Parameters("browser")
public void setUp(String browser) {
    DriverManager.setDriver(BrowserType.valueOf(browser.toUpperCase()));
    driver = DriverManager.getDriver();
    driver.get(config.get("url"));
}

Listeners

Screenshot on Failure

public class TestListener implements ITestListener {
    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        String path = ScreenshotUtils.capture(DriverManager.getDriver(), result.getName());
        ExtentReportManager.getTest().addScreenCaptureFromPath(path);
    }
}

Retry Failed Tests

public class RetryAnalyzer implements IRetryAnalyzer {
    private int count = 0;
    private static final int MAX = 2;

    @Override
    public boolean retry(ITestResult result) {
        if (count < MAX) { count++; return true; }
        return false;
    }
}

// Usage: @Test(retryAnalyzer = RetryAnalyzer.class)

Custom Reporting

@Override
public void onFinish(ITestContext context) {
    ExtentReportManager.flushReport();
}

Groups — Smoke / Regression

@Test(groups = {"smoke"})
public void validLogin() { /* ... */ }

@Test(groups = {"regression"})
public void invalidLogin() { /* ... */ }
<!-- testng.xml -->
<groups>
  <run>
    <include name="smoke"/>
    <exclude name="regression"/>
  </run>
</groups>

Complete Integration Example — LoginTest

package com.framework.tests;

import com.framework.base.BaseTest;
import com.framework.dataproviders.LoginDataProvider;
import com.framework.listeners.RetryAnalyzer;
import com.framework.pages.HomePage;
import com.framework.pages.LoginPage;
import org.testng.Assert;
import org.testng.annotations.Test;
import org.testng.asserts.SoftAssert;

public class LoginTest extends BaseTest {

    @Test(dataProvider = "loginData", dataProviderClass = LoginDataProvider.class,
          groups = {"smoke"}, retryAnalyzer = RetryAnalyzer.class,
          description = "Verify login with valid and invalid credentials")
    public void testLogin(String username, String password, boolean expectedSuccess) {
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage();

        if (expectedSuccess) {
            HomePage home = loginPage.login(username, password);
            SoftAssert soft = new SoftAssert();
            soft.assertTrue(home.isDashboardDisplayed(), "Dashboard not displayed");
            soft.assertEquals(home.getWelcomeText(), "Welcome, " + username + "!");
            soft.assertAll();
        } else {
            loginPage.login(username, password);
            Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getErrorMessage().contains("Invalid"),
                "Expected error message not shown");
        }
    }

    @Test(groups = {"regression"}, dependsOnGroups = {"smoke"})
    public void testLogout() {
        new LoginPage().login("admin", "admin123");
        HomePage home = new HomePage();
        home.clickLogout();
        Assert.assertTrue(new LoginPage().isLoginPageDisplayed());
    }
}

Interview Q&A (10+)

#QuestionAnswer
1Why TestNG over JUnit for Selenium?Better parallel, groups, DataProvider, listeners, XML suites.
2@BeforeMethod vs @BeforeClass?BeforeMethod runs before each test; BeforeClass once per class.
3What is @DataProvider?Supplies multiple data sets to a single @Test method.
4Hard vs Soft assert?Hard stops immediately; Soft collects failures, reports at assertAll().
5How to run tests in parallel?testng.xml parallel="tests" thread-count="N" + ThreadLocal driver.
6Why ThreadLocal WebDriver?Prevents driver sharing across parallel threads.
7What are TestNG groups?Tag tests (smoke/regression); include/exclude in XML.
8How to retry failed tests?Implement IRetryAnalyzer, attach via @Test(retryAnalyzer=...).
9What is ITestListener?Interface for test lifecycle hooks — failure screenshots, reporting.
10@Parameters vs @DataProvider?Parameters from XML (static); DataProvider from method (dynamic).
11dependsOnGroups usage?Run test only after specified groups pass.
12How to pass browser to tests?@Parameters in testng.xml + @BeforeMethod @Parameters("browser").

Section 31: Selenium + Cucumber BDD

Why Cucumber with Selenium?

Behavior-Driven Development (BDD) bridges the gap between business stakeholders and automation engineers. Cucumber reads plain-English Gherkin scenarios and maps them to Selenium step definitions, making tests readable by product owners, BA, and QA alike.

  • Business-readable: Scenarios describe user behavior, not Java syntax.
  • Collaboration: Three Amigos (BA, Dev, QA) define acceptance criteria together.
  • Living documentation: Feature files stay in sync with the application and serve as executable specs.
Key Idea: Gherkin describes what the user does; step definitions describe how Selenium performs it.

BDD Framework Architecture

Feature File (.feature)
        │
        ▼
Step Definitions (Java + Selenium)
        │
        ▼
Test Runner (TestNG / JUnit)
        │
        ▼
HTML / JSON Report (Cucumber Reports / Extent / Allure)

Framework Folder Structure

automation-framework/
├── src/test/java/
│   ├── features/              # .feature files (Gherkin)
│   │   └── login.feature
│   ├── stepdefinitions/
│   │   └── LoginSteps.java
│   ├── hooks/
│   │   └── Hooks.java
│   ├── pages/
│   │   └── LoginPage.java
│   ├── runners/
│   │   └── TestRunner.java
│   └── context/
│       └── TestContext.java
├── src/test/resources/
│   └── config.properties
└── pom.xml

Complete Working Example

1. login.feature — 4 Scenarios

Feature: User Login
  As a registered user
  I want to log in to the application
  So that I can access my dashboard

  Background:
    Given the user is on the login page

  @smoke @positive
  Scenario: Successful login with valid credentials
    When the user enters username "john.doe@example.com" and password "SecurePass123"
    And clicks the login button
    Then the user should see the dashboard
    And the welcome message should contain "Welcome, John"

  @negative
  Scenario: Login fails with invalid password
    When the user enters username "john.doe@example.com" and password "wrongpass"
    And clicks the login button
    Then an error message "Invalid credentials" should be displayed

  @negative
  Scenario Outline: Login fails with invalid data
    When the user enters username "<username>" and password "<password>"
    And clicks the login button
    Then an error message "<error>" should be displayed

    Examples:
      | username              | password    | error                  |
      |                       | SecurePass  | Username is required   |
      | john.doe@example.com  |             | Password is required   |
      | invalid-email         | SecurePass  | Invalid email format   |

  @regression
  Scenario: Remember me checkbox persists session
    When the user enters username "john.doe@example.com" and password "SecurePass123"
    And checks the remember me checkbox
    And clicks the login button
    Then the user should see the dashboard
    And the session cookie should be present

2. LoginPage.java — Page Object

package pages;

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.FindBy;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.PageFactory;

public class LoginPage {
    private WebDriver driver;

    @FindBy(id = "username")
    private WebElement usernameField;

    @FindBy(id = "password")
    private WebElement passwordField;

    @FindBy(id = "login-btn")
    private WebElement loginButton;

    @FindBy(id = "remember-me")
    private WebElement rememberMeCheckbox;

    @FindBy(css = ".error-message")
    private WebElement errorMessage;

    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    public void navigateTo(String url) {
        driver.get(url);
    }

    public void enterUsername(String username) {
        usernameField.clear();
        usernameField.sendKeys(username);
    }

    public void enterPassword(String password) {
        passwordField.clear();
        passwordField.sendKeys(password);
    }

    public void clickLogin() {
        loginButton.click();
    }

    public void checkRememberMe() {
        if (!rememberMeCheckbox.isSelected()) {
            rememberMeCheckbox.click();
        }
    }

    public String getErrorMessage() {
        return errorMessage.getText();
    }

    public boolean isErrorDisplayed() {
        return errorMessage.isDisplayed();
    }
}

3. LoginSteps.java — Step Definitions

package stepdefinitions;

import context.TestContext;
import io.cucumber.java.en.*;
import org.testng.Assert;
import pages.DashboardPage;
import pages.LoginPage;

public class LoginSteps {
    private TestContext context;
    private LoginPage loginPage;
    private DashboardPage dashboardPage;

    public LoginSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
    }

    @Given("the user is on the login page")
    public void userIsOnLoginPage() {
        loginPage = new LoginPage(context.getDriver());
        loginPage.navigateTo(context.getBaseUrl() + "/login");
    }

    @When("the user enters username {string} and password {string}")
    public void enterCredentials(String username, String password) {
        loginPage.enterUsername(username);
        loginPage.enterPassword(password);
    }

    @When("clicks the login button")
    public void clickLoginButton() {
        loginPage.clickLogin();
    }

    @When("checks the remember me checkbox")
    public void checkRememberMe() {
        loginPage.checkRememberMe();
    }

    @Then("the user should see the dashboard")
    public void verifyDashboard() {
        dashboardPage = new DashboardPage(context.getDriver());
        Assert.assertTrue(dashboardPage.isDashboardDisplayed());
    }

    @Then("the welcome message should contain {string}")
    public void verifyWelcomeMessage(String expected) {
        Assert.assertTrue(dashboardPage.getWelcomeMessage().contains(expected));
    }

    @Then("an error message {string} should be displayed")
    public void verifyErrorMessage(String expected) {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.isErrorDisplayed());
        Assert.assertEquals(loginPage.getErrorMessage(), expected);
    }

    @Then("the session cookie should be present")
    public void verifySessionCookie() {
        Assert.assertNotNull(context.getDriver().manage().getCookieNamed("SESSIONID"));
    }
}

4. Hooks.java — @Before / @After

package hooks;

import context.TestContext;
import io.cucumber.java.After;
import io.cucumber.java.Before;
import io.cucumber.java.Scenario;
import org.openqa.selenium.OutputType;
import org.openqa.selenium.TakesScreenshot;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeOptions;
import java.time.Duration;

public class Hooks {
    private TestContext context;

    public Hooks(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
    }

    @Before
    public void setUp(Scenario scenario) {
        ChromeOptions options = new ChromeOptions();
        options.addArguments("--start-maximized");
        WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver(options);
        driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(Duration.ofSeconds(10));
        context.setDriver(driver);
        context.setBaseUrl("https://app.example.com");
    }

    @After
    public void tearDown(Scenario scenario) {
        if (scenario.isFailed()) {
            byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) context.getDriver())
                .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
            scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", scenario.getName());
        }
        if (context.getDriver() != null) {
            context.getDriver().quit();
        }
    }
}

5. TestRunner.java — TestNG Runner

package runners;

import io.cucumber.testng.AbstractTestNGCucumberTests;
import io.cucumber.testng.CucumberOptions;
import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;

@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/java/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    plugin = {
        "pretty",
        "html:target/cucumber-report.html",
        "json:target/cucumber-report.json",
        "com.aventstack.extentreports.cucumber.adapter.ExtentCucumberAdapter:"
    },
    tags = "@smoke or @regression",
    monochrome = true
)
public class TestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests {

    @Override
    @DataProvider(parallel = true)
    public Object[][] scenarios() {
        return super.scenarios();
    }
}

Sharing State: TestContext / ScenarioContext Pattern

Cucumber creates a new step definition instance per scenario by default. Use a shared context object injected via PicoContainer or manual constructor injection to pass WebDriver and test data between steps.

package context;

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;

public class TestContext {
    private WebDriver driver;
    private String baseUrl;

    public WebDriver getDriver() { return driver; }
    public void setDriver(WebDriver driver) { this.driver = driver; }
    public String getBaseUrl() { return baseUrl; }
    public void setBaseUrl(String baseUrl) { this.baseUrl = baseUrl; }
}
Dependency Injection: Add cucumber-picocontainer to pom.xml. Cucumber auto-wires classes with shared constructor parameters.

Cucumber + Selenium Best Practices

  1. Keep steps reusable: One step = one action. Avoid scenario-specific step text.
  2. Use Page Objects: Step definitions should delegate to POM, not contain locators.
  3. Tag strategically: @smoke, @regression, @wip for selective execution.
  4. Avoid technical language in Gherkin: Write "clicks login" not "clicks element by id login-btn".
  5. One scenario = one behavior: Do not chain unrelated validations in a single scenario.
  6. Use Background for common setup: Reduce duplication across scenarios in a feature.
  7. Attach screenshots on failure: Use @After hook with scenario.attach().
  8. Parallel execution carefully: Use ThreadLocal WebDriver with PicoContainer scoped per scenario.

BDD Anti-Patterns with Selenium

Anti-PatternProblemFix
Imperative Gherkin"Given I open Chrome, When I find element by xpath..."Describe behavior, not implementation
God Step DefinitionsOne step does login + navigation + assertionSplit into atomic reusable steps
Duplicate step textSame action with 5 different step phrasesConsolidate to one canonical step
Locators in feature filesXPath in GherkinKeep locators in Page Objects only
Testing through UI onlyUI setup for data that API can createUse API for test data, UI for validation
Overloaded Examples tables50-row Scenario OutlineUse DataProvider or external CSV for bulk data

Interview Questions & Answers

#QuestionAnswer
1What is Cucumber?A BDD tool that executes Gherkin scenarios mapped to step definition methods.
2What is Gherkin?Plain-text language with Given/When/Then keywords for describing behavior.
3How does Cucumber find step definitions?Via the glue package in @CucumberOptions — scans for annotation-matched methods.
4Background vs Before hook?Background is Gherkin-level shared steps; @Before is Java setup before each scenario.
5Scenario vs Scenario Outline?Scenario is single flow; Outline runs multiple times with Examples table.
6How to share WebDriver between steps?TestContext with dependency injection (PicoContainer) or static ThreadLocal.
7How to run specific tags?tags = "@smoke" in runner or -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke" via Maven.
8Cucumber with TestNG or JUnit?Both supported; extend AbstractTestNGCucumberTests for TestNG integration.
9What is dry-run?Validates feature-to-step mapping without executing browser actions.
10How to attach screenshot on failure?In @After hook: check scenario.isFailed(), call scenario.attach(bytes, mime, name).
11What is PicoContainer in Cucumber?DI library enabling shared state between step definition classes.
12Can one step match multiple annotations?Yes, but avoid ambiguity — each Gherkin phrase must map to exactly one method.

Section 32: Selenium + Maven

What Is Maven?

Apache Maven is a build automation and dependency management tool for Java projects. It uses a Project Object Model (POM) to define project structure, libraries, plugins, and build lifecycle — eliminating manual JAR management.

  • Build automation: Compile, test, package, and deploy with standardized commands.
  • Dependency management: Auto-downloads transitive dependencies from Maven Central.
  • Convention over configuration: Standard directory layout (src/main/java, src/test/java).

Standard Project Structure

selenium-framework/
├── pom.xml
├── src/
│   ├── main/java/          # Framework utilities (optional)
│   └── test/
│       ├── java/           # Test classes, Page Objects, listeners
│       └── resources/      # config files, testng.xml, log4j2.xml
└── target/                 # Compiled classes, reports (auto-generated)

pom.xml Anatomy

Coordinates: groupId, artifactId, version

<groupId>com.mycompany</groupId>
<artifactId>selenium-automation</artifactId>
<version>1.0.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
<packaging>jar</packaging>

Properties — Java Version & Compiler

<properties>
    <maven.compiler.source>17</maven.compiler.source>
    <maven.compiler.target>17</maven.compiler.target>
    <project.build.sourceEncoding>UTF-8</project.build.sourceEncoding>
    <selenium.version>4.18.1</selenium.version>
    <testng.version>7.9.0</testng.version>
</properties>

Complete pom.xml for Automation Framework

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
         http://maven.apache.org/xsd/maven-4.0.0.xsd">
    <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>

    <groupId>com.mycompany</groupId>
    <artifactId>selenium-framework</artifactId>
    <version>1.0.0-SNAPSHOT</version>

    <properties>
        <maven.compiler.source>17</maven.compiler.source>
        <maven.compiler.target>17</maven.compiler.target>
        <selenium.version>4.18.1</selenium.version>
        <testng.version>7.9.0</testng.version>
        <webdrivermanager.version>5.7.0</webdrivermanager.version>
        <extentreports.version>5.1.1</extentreports.version>
        <poi.version>5.2.5</poi.version>
        <log4j.version>2.22.1</log4j.version>
    </properties>

    <dependencies>
        <!-- Selenium -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.seleniumhq.selenium</groupId>
            <artifactId>selenium-java</artifactId>
            <version>${selenium.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <!-- TestNG -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.testng</groupId>
            <artifactId>testng</artifactId>
            <version>${testng.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <!-- WebDriverManager -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>io.github.bonigarcia</groupId>
            <artifactId>webdrivermanager</artifactId>
            <version>${webdrivermanager.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <!-- Extent Reports -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>com.aventstack</groupId>
            <artifactId>extentreports</artifactId>
            <version>${extentreports.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <!-- Apache POI (Excel) -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.apache.poi</groupId>
            <artifactId>poi-ooxml</artifactId>
            <version>${poi.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <!-- Log4j2 -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.apache.logging.log4j</groupId>
            <artifactId>log4j-core</artifactId>
            <version>${log4j.version}</version>
        </dependency>
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.apache.logging.log4j</groupId>
            <artifactId>log4j-api</artifactId>
            <version>${log4j.version}</version>
        </dependency>
    </dependencies>

    <build>
        <plugins>
            <plugin>
                <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
                <artifactId>maven-compiler-plugin</artifactId>
                <version>3.12.1</version>
                <configuration>
                    <source>17</source>
                    <target>17</target>
                </configuration>
            </plugin>
            <plugin>
                <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
                <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
                <version>3.2.5</version>
                <configuration>
                    <suiteXmlFiles>
                        <suiteXmlFile>src/test/resources/testng.xml</suiteXmlFile>
                    </suiteXmlFiles>
                    <parallel>methods</parallel>
                    <threadCount>3</threadCount>
                    <systemPropertyVariables>
                        <browser>${browser}</browser>
                        <env>${env}</env>
                    </systemPropertyVariables>
                </configuration>
            </plugin>
        </plugins>
    </build>

    <profiles>
        <profile>
            <id>dev</id>
            <properties><env>dev</env><base.url>https://dev.example.com</base.url></properties>
        </profile>
        <profile>
            <id>qa</id>
            <activation><activeByDefault>true</activeByDefault></activation>
            <properties><env>qa</env><base.url>https://qa.example.com</base.url></properties>
        </profile>
        <profile>
            <id>staging</id>
            <properties><env>staging</env><base.url>https://staging.example.com</base.url></properties>
        </profile>
        <profile>
            <id>prod</id>
            <properties><env>prod</env><base.url>https://example.com</base.url></properties>
        </profile>
    </profiles>
</project>

Maven Lifecycle

validate → compile → test → package → verify → install → deploy
   │          │         │        │                    │
   │          │         │        │                    └─ Deploy to remote repo
   │          │         │        └─ Create JAR/WAR
   │          │         └─ Run tests (Surefire)
   │          └─ Compile source code
   └─ Validate POM structure

Essential Maven Commands

CommandDescription
mvn cleanDeletes the target/ directory
mvn compileCompiles main source code
mvn testCompiles test code and runs all tests
mvn clean testClean build + run all tests
mvn test -Dtest=LoginTestRun a specific test class
mvn test -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=smoke.xmlRun a specific TestNG suite
mvn test -Dbrowser=chrome -Denv=qaPass system properties to tests
mvn installPackage and install to local .m2 repository
mvn dependency:treeDisplay dependency hierarchy
mvn test -PstagingActivate staging profile

Maven Surefire Plugin

Surefire executes unit and integration tests during the test phase. Key configurations:

  • testng.xml integration: <suiteXmlFiles> points to TestNG suite
  • Parallel execution: <parallel>methods</parallel> with <threadCount>3</threadCount>
  • Includes/excludes: <includes><include>**/*Test.java</include></includes>

.m2 Repository & settings.xml

Maven stores downloaded dependencies in ~/.m2/repository. Customize mirrors, credentials, and proxy in ~/.m2/settings.xml:

<settings>
    <mirrors>
        <mirror>
            <id>corporate-nexus</id>
            <mirrorOf>central</mirrorOf>
            <url>https://nexus.company.com/repository/maven-public</url>
        </mirror>
    </mirrors>
    <profiles>
        <profile>
            <id>corporate</id>
            <repositories>
                <repository>
                    <id>central</id>
                    <url>https://nexus.company.com/repository/maven-public</url>
                </repository>
            </repositories>
        </profile>
    </profiles>
    <activeProfiles>
        <activeProfile>corporate</activeProfile>
    </activeProfiles>
</settings>

Interview Questions & Answers

#QuestionAnswer
1What is pom.xml?Project Object Model — XML file defining project metadata, dependencies, and build config.
2groupId vs artifactId?groupId = organization (com.company); artifactId = project name (selenium-tests).
3What is Maven Central?Default public repository hosting Java libraries at repo.maven.apache.org.
4How to pass parameters to tests?-Dproperty=value read via System.getProperty() or @Parameters.
5What is Surefire plugin?Runs tests during Maven test phase; integrates with TestNG/JUnit.
6What are Maven profiles?Environment-specific config blocks activated by -P flag or conditions.
7clean vs clean install?clean deletes target; install also packages and copies to local .m2 repo.
8How to skip tests?mvn install -DskipTests (compile tests) or -Dmaven.test.skip=true (skip compilation).
9What is dependency:tree?Shows transitive dependency hierarchy to debug version conflicts.
10SNAPSHOT vs RELEASE version?SNAPSHOT is development (auto-updated); RELEASE is immutable production version.
11How to run parallel tests via Maven?Configure surefire-plugin with parallel and threadCount properties.
12Where are JARs stored locally?~/.m2/repository/<groupId>/<artifactId>/<version>/

Section 33: Selenium + Jenkins CI/CD

CI/CD Pipeline for Selenium

Continuous Integration automatically builds and tests code on every commit. Continuous Delivery extends this to deploy validated builds. For Selenium, CI/CD ensures regression runs on schedule and after every push.

Developer Push
      │
      ▼
   GitHub (Webhook)
      │
      ▼
   Jenkins Job Triggered
      │
      ├── Checkout Code
      ├── Maven Build (mvn clean compile)
      ├── Run Tests (mvn test -Dsuite=smoke.xml)
      ├── Generate Reports (Extent / Allure / TestNG)
      └── Notification (Email / Slack)
            │
            ▼
      Pass ✅  or  Fail ❌

Jenkins Job Configuration

1. Freestyle Project — Step-by-Step

  1. Create New Item → Freestyle project → name: Selenium-Regression
  2. Source Code Management → Git → Repository URL + credentials
  3. Build Triggers → Poll SCM or GitHub hook trigger
  4. Build Environment → Delete workspace before build (optional)
  5. Build Steps → Invoke top-level Maven targets: clean test -Dbrowser=chrome -Denv=qa
  6. Post-build Actions → Publish TestNG Results, Publish HTML reports, Email notification

2. Pipeline Project — Jenkinsfile (Preferred)

Pipeline-as-Code version-controls the entire CI/CD definition alongside test code. Supports parameters, parallel stages, and conditional logic.

Complete Jenkinsfile

pipeline {
    agent any

    parameters {
        choice(name: 'BROWSER', choices: ['chrome', 'firefox', 'edge'], description: 'Browser to run tests')
        choice(name: 'ENVIRONMENT', choices: ['qa', 'staging', 'prod'], description: 'Target environment')
        choice(name: 'SUITE', choices: ['smoke', 'regression', 'full'], description: 'Test suite to execute')
    }

    environment {
        MAVEN_HOME = tool 'Maven-3.9'
        JAVA_HOME = tool 'JDK-17'
        PATH = "${MAVEN_HOME}/bin:${JAVA_HOME}/bin:${PATH}"
    }

    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps {
                git branch: 'main', url: 'https://github.com/myorg/selenium-framework.git'
            }
        }
        stage('Build') {
            steps {
                bat 'mvn clean compile -DskipTests'
            }
        }
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                bat "mvn test -Dbrowser=${params.BROWSER} -Denv=${params.ENVIRONMENT} -Dsurefire.suiteXmlFiles=src/test/resources/${params.SUITE}.xml"
            }
        }
        stage('Report') {
            steps {
                publishHTML(target: [
                    allowMissing: false,
                    alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true,
                    keepAll: true,
                    reportDir: 'target/extent-reports',
                    reportFiles: 'index.html',
                    reportName: 'Extent Report'
                ])
                junit 'target/surefire-reports/*.xml'
            }
        }
    }

    post {
        always {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'target/**/*-report*.html, target/screenshots/**', allowEmptyArchive: true
            emailext(
                subject: "Build ${env.BUILD_NUMBER} - ${currentBuild.currentResult}",
                body: "Test run on ${params.ENVIRONMENT} with ${params.BROWSER}. See ${env.BUILD_URL}",
                to: 'qa-team@company.com'
            )
        }
        failure {
            slackSend(channel: '#automation-alerts',
                color: 'danger',
                message: "❌ Selenium build FAILED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}")
        }
        success {
            slackSend(channel: '#automation-alerts',
                color: 'good',
                message: "✅ Selenium build PASSED: ${env.JOB_NAME} #${env.BUILD_NUMBER}")
        }
    }
}

Essential Jenkins Plugins for Selenium

PluginPurpose
Git PluginClone repository from GitHub/GitLab/Bitbucket
Maven IntegrationConfigure Maven installations and run mvn targets
TestNG ResultsParse and display TestNG XML results in Jenkins UI
HTML PublisherPublish Extent/custom HTML reports as build artifacts
Allure PluginGenerate and display Allure report from allure-results
Email ExtensionCustomizable email notifications with templates
Slack NotificationSend build status to Slack channels
PipelineEnable Jenkinsfile-based pipeline jobs

Scheduled Builds — Cron Syntax

triggers {
    cron('H 2 * * 1-5')  // Nightly at ~2 AM, Mon-Fri
    cron('0 6 * * 0')    // Full regression every Sunday 6 AM
}
Cron format: MINUTE HOUR DOM MONTH DOW. Use H for hash-based distribution to avoid load spikes.

Parameterized Builds

Allow QA to select browser, environment, and suite at build time without editing code. Parameters appear on the Build with Parameters page.

Jenkins + Docker — Containerized Execution

stage('Test in Docker') {
    agent {
        docker {
            image 'selenium/standalone-chrome:4.18.1'
            args '-v /dev/shm:/dev/shm --network host'
        }
    }
    steps {
        sh 'mvn test -Dbrowser=remote -Dgrid.url=http://localhost:4444'
    }
}

Email Notification Template

emailext(
    subject: '${PROJECT_NAME} - Build #${BUILD_NUMBER} - ${BUILD_STATUS}',
    body: '''
        <h2>Selenium Test Results</h2>
        <p>Job: ${PROJECT_NAME}</p>
        <p>Build: #${BUILD_NUMBER}</p>
        <p>Status: ${BUILD_STATUS}</p>
        <p>Browser: ${BROWSER} | Environment: ${ENVIRONMENT}</p>
        <p><a href="${BUILD_URL}">View Build</a></p>
        <p><a href="${BUILD_URL}Extent_20Report/">View Report</a></p>
    ''',
    to: 'qa-team@company.com',
    mimeType: 'text/html'
)

Webhook Triggers — GitHub Push → Auto Build

  1. GitHub repo → Settings → Webhooks → Add webhook
  2. Payload URL: http://jenkins-server:8080/github-webhook/
  3. Content type: application/json; Events: Push, Pull Request
  4. Jenkins job → Build Triggers → GitHub hook trigger for GITScm polling

Interview Questions & Answers

#QuestionAnswer
1What is CI/CD?CI automates build/test on commit; CD automates deployment to environments.
2Freestyle vs Pipeline?Freestyle is UI-configured; Pipeline uses Jenkinsfile as code (version-controlled).
3How to pass Maven params in Jenkins?Build step: mvn test -Dbrowser=chrome or use parameterized pipeline.
4How to publish TestNG results?Post-build: Publish TestNG Results → target/surefire-reports/*.xml
5What is Jenkins agent?Execution node (master or slave) where pipeline stages run.
6How to schedule nightly builds?Pipeline triggers { cron('H 2 * * *') } or Poll SCM in freestyle.
7How to archive test reports?post { always { archiveArtifacts 'target/reports/**' } }
8Can Jenkins run tests in Docker?Yes — use docker agent in pipeline stage with Selenium image.
9What is Blue Ocean?Jenkins modern UI for visualizing pipeline stages and logs.
10How to trigger build on PR merge?GitHub webhook + multibranch pipeline detecting branch changes.
11How to handle test failures in pipeline?post { failure { ... } } block for notifications; junit step marks build unstable.
12What is credentials binding?Securely inject secrets (passwords, tokens) via Jenkins Credentials plugin.

Section 34: Reporting in Selenium

TestNG Default Reports

TestNG auto-generates reports in test-output/ after every run:

  • test-output/index.html — Full suite results with pass/fail/skip counts
  • test-output/emailable-report.html — Lightweight summary for email sharing
Limitations: Basic styling, no screenshots, no step-level logging, limited customization without listeners.

Extent Reports

ExtentReports is the most popular custom reporting library for Selenium. ExtentSparkReporter generates rich HTML reports with charts, screenshots, and categories.

Setup: ExtentReports + ExtentSparkReporter

import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentTest;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.reporter.ExtentSparkReporter;

ExtentSparkReporter spark = new ExtentSparkReporter("target/extent-reports/index.html");
ExtentReports extent = new ExtentReports();
extent.attachReporter(spark);
ExtentTest test = extent.createTest("Login Test");
test.pass("Login successful");
extent.flush();

Complete ExtentReportManager Class

package reports;

import com.aventstack.extentreports.*;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.reporter.ExtentSparkReporter;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.reporter.configuration.Theme;

public class ExtentReportManager {
    private static ExtentReports extent;
    private static ThreadLocal<ExtentTest> test = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static ExtentReports getInstance() {
        if (extent == null) {
            ExtentSparkReporter spark = new ExtentSparkReporter("target/extent-reports/index.html");
            spark.config().setTheme(Theme.STANDARD);
            spark.config().setDocumentTitle("Automation Report");
            spark.config().setReportName("Selenium Test Results");
            spark.config().setTimeStampFormat("dd-MM-yyyy HH:mm:ss");

            extent = new ExtentReports();
            extent.attachReporter(spark);
            extent.setSystemInfo("OS", System.getProperty("os.name"));
            extent.setSystemInfo("Java", System.getProperty("java.version"));
            extent.setSystemInfo("Browser", System.getProperty("browser", "chrome"));
        }
        return extent;
    }

    public static void startTest(String name, String description) {
        ExtentTest extentTest = getInstance().createTest(name, description);
        test.set(extentTest);
    }

    public static ExtentTest getTest() { return test.get(); }

    public static void flush() { getInstance().flush(); }
}

Logging Methods

ExtentTest test = ExtentReportManager.getTest();
test.info("Navigated to login page");
test.pass("Credentials entered successfully");
test.warning("Slow page load detected");
test.fail("Login failed - element not found");
test.skip("Test skipped due to dependency failure");

Screenshots in Extent

public static String captureScreenshot(WebDriver driver, String name) {
    String path = "target/screenshots/" + name + ".png";
    File src = ((TakesScreenshot) driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
    FileUtils.copyFile(src, new File(path));
    return path;
}

// In listener on test failure:
ExtentReportManager.getTest()
    .fail("Test failed")
    .addScreenCaptureFromPath(captureScreenshot(driver, testName));

TestNG ITestListener Integration

public class ExtentTestListener implements ITestListener {
    @Override
    public void onTestStart(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentReportManager.startTest(
            result.getMethod().getMethodName(),
            result.getMethod().getDescription()
        );
    }
    @Override
    public void onTestSuccess(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentReportManager.getTest().pass("Test passed");
    }
    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentReportManager.getTest().fail(result.getThrowable());
    }
    @Override
    public void onFinish(ITestContext context) {
        ExtentReportManager.flush();
    }
}

Interview Questions & Answers

#QuestionAnswer
1Where are TestNG reports generated?test-output/index.html and emailable-report.html
2What is ExtentSparkReporter?HTML reporter for ExtentReports 5.x generating interactive reports.
3How to add screenshot to Extent report?test.fail().addScreenCaptureFromPath(path) in ITestListener on failure.
4What is ITestListener?TestNG interface with callbacks: onTestStart, onTestSuccess, onTestFailure, onFinish.
5How to generate Allure report?Run tests → allure serve target/allure-results
6@Step vs test.info()?@Step auto-logs method calls in Allure; test.info() is manual Extent logging.
7Why ThreadLocal for ExtentTest?Parallel execution requires isolated report instances per thread.
8Log4j vs System.out.println?Log4j supports levels, file appenders, formatting, and production-grade logging.
9How to customize Extent report theme?spark.config().setTheme(Theme.DARK) or spark-config.xml
10Can you combine Extent and Allure?Yes, but usually pick one primary HTML reporter to avoid duplication.
11What is extent.flush()?Writes buffered report data to disk — call in @AfterSuite or onFinish.
12How to categorize tests in Extent?test.assignCategory("Smoke", "Login") for filtered report views.

Section 35: Selenium Grid

What Is Selenium Grid?

Selenium Grid enables distributed test execution across multiple machines and browsers simultaneously. A Hub receives test requests and routes them to registered Nodes that launch browsers — dramatically reducing total execution time for large regression suites.

Selenium Grid 4 Architecture

                    ┌──────────┐
   Test Script ────►│  Router  │ (Entry point :4444)
                    └────┬─────┘
                         │
              ┌──────────┼──────────┐
              ▼          ▼          ▼
        ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐
        │Session   │ │Distributor│ │Event Bus │
        │Queue     │ │          │ │ (Redis)  │
        └──────────┘ └────┬─────┘ └──────────┘
                          │
              ┌───────────┼───────────┐
              ▼           ▼           ▼
        ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐
        │ Node 1   │ │ Node 2   │ │ Node 3   │
        │ Chrome   │ │ Firefox  │ │ Edge     │
        └──────────┘ └──────────┘ └──────────┘

Components

  • Router: Single entry point receiving WebDriver requests
  • Distributor: Matches session requests to available nodes
  • Session Map: Tracks active sessions and their node assignments
  • Node: Machine running browsers; registers capabilities with hub
  • Event Bus: Internal communication channel between components

Deployment Modes

ModeDescriptionUse Case
StandaloneAll components in one processLocal development, small teams
Hub-NodeHub + separate node machinesMedium-scale parallel execution
Fully DistributedEach component as separate serviceLarge enterprise, Kubernetes

Grid 3 vs Grid 4 Comparison

FeatureGrid 3Grid 4
ArchitectureHub + Node onlyRouter, Distributor, Session Map, Event Bus
W3C ProtocolPartialFull W3C WebDriver compliance
ConfigurationJSON config filesTOML config + CLI flags
Docker supportManual setupOfficial Docker images
ObservabilityBasic logsGraphQL API + Web UI dashboard
Session queueBasicAdvanced queue with retry

Grid Setup Commands

# Download Selenium Server 4.x
# https://github.com/SeleniumHQ/selenium/releases

# Standalone mode (dev)
java -jar selenium-server-4.18.1.jar standalone

# Hub mode
java -jar selenium-server-4.18.1.jar hub --port 4444

# Node mode (register with hub)
java -jar selenium-server-4.18.1.jar node --hub http://192.168.1.100:4444

# Node with specific browsers
java -jar selenium-server-4.18.1.jar node --hub http://localhost:4444 \
  --detect-drivers true

RemoteWebDriver — Connecting Tests to Grid

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeOptions;
import org.openqa.selenium.remote.RemoteWebDriver;
import java.net.URL;

public class GridTest {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        ChromeOptions options = new ChromeOptions();
        options.addArguments("--start-maximized");

        WebDriver driver = new RemoteWebDriver(
            new URL("http://localhost:4444"),
            options  // Selenium 4: use Options instead of DesiredCapabilities
        );

        driver.get("https://example.com");
        System.out.println("Title: " + driver.getTitle());
        driver.quit();
    }
}
Selenium 4 Change: Replace DesiredCapabilities with browser-specific Options classes (ChromeOptions, FirefoxOptions, EdgeOptions).
